Yet fearing that later generations of arrogant and dissolute men might mistake illusion for reality and use the Dao as a pretext for villainy, I have excised such accounts.

As for the theory of the Sixteen Transformations, its details are obscure and offer no enlightenment.

In the first year of Emperor Qin Shi Huang, the yimao year (246 BCE), he reigned for thirty-six years, and in the gengchen year (221 BCE), he first unified the realm as emperor. In the twenty-eighth year, renwu (219 BCE), he performed the Feng and Shan sacrifices on Mount Tai and established a shrine to Lao Jun south of the Louguan Temple, personally conducting the rites. Lao Jun descended to the shrine and bestowed upon the emperor the *Ghostly Forest Scripture*, a talisman for commanding spirits and deities.

—From the *Louguan Tradition*

Emperor Wen of the Former Han...

In the first year, renxu (140 BCE), Lao Jun first descended upon the banks of the Shan River, where he was known as the River Master (Heshang Gong) or the River Elder (Heshang Zhangren). Emperor Wen personally sought him out, and Lao Jun bestowed upon him the *Scripture of the Dao and Its Virtue*. Today, north of Shanzhou Prefecture, the Temple of the River Master and Emperor Wen’s Terrace for Gazing at Immortals still stand. Recorded in the *Records of the Grand Historian* and Ge Hong’s *Biographies of Divine Transcendents*. Some texts mistakenly attribute this to Emperor Jing.

Emperor Cheng:
In the first year of the Heping era, guisi (28 BCE), and in the second year, jiawu (27 BCE), Lao Jun descended upon Quyang Abyss in Langye Prefecture, where he bestowed upon Gan Ji the *Scripture of Great Peace*. Recorded in the *Book of the Later Han*.

Emperor Ming of the Later Han:
Buddhist teachings first entered China.

Emperor Zhang:
In the first year of the Yuanhe era, jiashen (84 CE), and in the second year, yiyou (85 CE), Lao Jun descended once more, bestowing upon Gan Ji the Perfected One the One Hundred and Eighty Precepts.

Emperor An:
In the first year of the Yongchu era, dingwei (107 CE), and in the third year, jiyou (109 CE), Lao Jun descended upon Mount Tai, summoning Liu Tu, the Registrar of Jiangxia, to review and rectify the celestial registers of the realm. There, he revealed the principles of karmic retribution for transgressions and blessings. Recorded in the Tang *Rhapsody on the Record of the Sage* and the *Illustrated Manifestations of Responses*.

Emperor Shun.

In the first year of the Yongjian era, bingyin (126 CE), six years later the era was changed to Yangjia, then four years later in bingzi (140 CE) to Yonghe, six years later in renwu (142 CE) to Han’an, and two years later in jiashen (144 CE) to Jiankang.

In the first year of the Han’an era, renwu (142 CE), Lao Jun descended upon Mount Heming in Shu, bestowing upon the Celestial Master Zhang Daoling the *Secret Register of Orthodox Unity and Alliance威*. In the fifth month, he descended once more, granting the *Nine Hundred and Thirty Scrolls of the Qin-Qing Central Canon* and seventy scrolls of talismanic script.

In the first year of the Jiankang era, jiashen (144 CE), Lao Jun descended again upon Mount Yuntai in Hezhou, transmitting to the Celestial Master the Three Caverns’ scriptures in their entirety, along with the rites for the *Fast of Direct Offering* to deliver the nine generations of ancestors. Recorded in the *Biography of the Celestial Master* and the *Illustrated Shu Gazetteer*.

Emperor Huan:
In the first year of the Jianhe era, dinghai (147 CE), three years later in gengyin (149 CE) the era was changed to Heping, then one year later in xinmao (151 CE) to Yuanjia, two years later in guisi (153 CE) to Yongxing, two years later in yiwei (155 CE) to Yongshou, three years later in wuxu (158 CE) to Yanxi, and nine years later in dingwei (167 CE) to Yongkang.

In the first year of the Yongshou era, yiwei (155 CE), Lao Jun descended upon Chengdu, transmitting to the Celestial Master the method of the Northern Dipper for *Erasing Death and Inscribing Life*. The site of the Jade Bureau’s transformation in Chengdu Prefecture marks the location. He descended again upon Mount Lutang, bestowing the *Text for Subduing the Six Heavens and Beheading Demons*. Recorded in the *Biography of the Celestial Master* and the *Illustrated Shu Gazetteer*.

In the eighth year of the Yanxi era (165 CE), the Emperor dispatched envoys to Chen to sacrifice to Lao Jun, commanding Bian Shao to compose the stele inscription. In the ninth year (166 CE), the Emperor personally offered sacrifices to Lao Jun at the Zhuolong Palace, employing the music of the suburban sacrifices to Heaven. Both events are recorded in the *Records of the Later Han*.

Emperor Ling.

In the first year of the Jianning era (178 CE), four years later, in the renzi year (182 CE), the reign title was changed to Jiaping; six years after that, in the wuwu year (188 CE), it was changed to Guanghe; and six years thereafter, in the jiazi year (194 CE), it was changed to Zhongping.

In the second year of the Guanghe era (179 CE), Lao Jun descended upon Mount Tianbai, bestowing upon the immortal Ge Xuan the *Upper Clarity*, *Numinous Treasure*, and *Great Cavern* scriptures, along with the Three Registers and Seven Grades of Fasting Methods, the *Wheel of Admonitions and Precepts*, the *Scripture on Revolving the Spirit and Entering Samadhi*, and other texts. Recorded in the *Records of Mount Tiantai* and the *Biography of the Supreme Ultimate Immortal Barge*.

During the first year of the Xianxi era (264 CE) of Chen Tu, King of Wei, Lao Jun descended upon Lin Tao Prefecture in Longyou, declaring to Wang Shi: "The world shall soon attain Great Peace." Recorded in the *Book of Jin*.

During the first year of the Long’an era (397 CE) of Emperor An of Jin, five years later, in the renyin year (402 CE), the reign title was changed to Yuanxing; three years after that, in the yisi year (405 CE), it was changed to Yixi.

In the first year of the Yuanxing era (402 CE), the fifth year of Hong Shi of the Later Qin, Lao Jun descended, inspecting the mountains and peaks. Upon reaching Mount Hua, he commanded the immortal Cheng Gongxing to relocate to Mount Song, bestowing upon him elixirs of immortality. Recorded in the *Book of the Later Wei*.

Emperor Ming of the Later Wei.

In the first year of the Yongxing era (409 CE), he ascended the throne; in the fifteenth year, the reign title was changed to Shenrui; two years later, it was changed to Taichang.

In the second year of the Shenrui era (415 CE), the yimao year, the eleventh year of the Yixi era of Emperor An of Jin, Lao Jun descended upon Mount Song, bestowing upon the Daoist Kou Qianzhi the *Yunzhong Yinsong Xinke Zhijie* (Precepts of the New Code Chanted in the Clouds). In the second year of the Taichang era (417 CE), the dingsi year, Lao Jun descended again, granting Kou Qianzhi seventy scrolls of talismans and registers. Recorded in the *Daoist and Buddhist Records of the Later Wei*.

Emperor Taiwu of the Later Wei.

In the first year of the Taiping era (440 CE), Lao Jun descended upon Mount Song, commanding Kou Qianzhi to confer upon the emperor the title of *Taiping Zhenjun* (True Lord of Great Peace), whereupon the reign title was changed to Taiping Zhenjun. Recorded in the *Book of Wei*.

Emperor Yang of Sui.

In the first year of the Daye era (605 CE), the yichou year. In the thirteenth year of the Daye era (617 CE), the dingchou year, Lao Jun descended upon Mount Zhongnan, revealing to the mountain recluse Li Chunfeng the celestial mandate of the Duke of Tang. Recorded in the *Record of the Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl*.

Emperor Gaozu of Tang.

In the first year of the Wude era (618 CE), the wuyin year. In the second year of the Wude era (619 CE), the jimao year, Lao Jun descended upon Mount Yangjiao, instructing Ji Shanxing to memorialize: "I am the imperial ancestor; now the Tang has attained sagely governance, and the altars of soil and grain shall endure." Recorded in the *Annals of Tang*.

In the wawu year (622 CE), Lao Jun descended again at the temple site, foretelling the time of the rebels' defeat. Recorded in the *Annals of Tang*.

Emperor Gaozong.

In the first year of the Yonghui era (650 CE), the gengxu year. Seven years later, in the bingchen year (656 CE), the era name was changed to Xianqing. Five years thereafter, in the xinyou year (661 CE), it was changed to Longshuo. Three years later, in the jiazi year (664 CE), it was changed to Linde. Two years thereafter, in the bingyin year (666 CE), it was changed to Qianfeng. Two years later, in the wuchen year (668 CE), it was changed to Zongzhang. Two years thereafter, in the gengwu year (670 CE), it was changed to Xianheng. Four years later, in the Jiaxu year (674 CE), it was changed to Shangyuan. Two years thereafter, in the bingzi year (676 CE), it was changed to Yifeng. Three years later, in the jimao year (679 CE), it was changed to Tiaolu. One year thereafter, in the gengchen year (680 CE), it was changed to Yonglong. One year later, in the xinsi year (681 CE), it was changed to Kaiyao. One year thereafter, in the renwu year (682 CE), it was changed to Yunchun.

In the second year of the Longshuo era (662 CE), the renxu year, the Emperor visited the palace at Luoyang and established a purified temple at the northern Deng district to worship Lao Jun, where a grand jiao offering was held in celebration. Lao Jun descended upon the palace hall, flanked by two Perfected Ones, their radiance illuminating the steps and altar, witnessed by all present. Palace Attendant Quan Dali and others recorded the event in memorials, and the auspicious image was depicted according to the vision. Recorded in the *Luoyang Records* and the memorial of Master Yang Hu.

In the first year of the Qianfeng era (666 CE), the bingyin year, the Emperor performed the Feng sacrifice at Mount Tai. His procession reached Bo, where he paid homage to Lao Jun, presenting an imperial decree and bestowing the august title of *Xuanyuan Emperor* upon him, while honoring his sagely mother as *Xiantian Empress Dowager*. Recorded in the *Annals of Tang*.

In the third year of the Yifeng era (678 CE), the wuyin year, the Emperor decreed a grand fast to be held at the Yangqing Temple. At that time, Lao Jun descended upon the altar, his auspicious light illuminating all, riding a white horse whose hooves left imprints upon the altar stones, witnessed by the assembled multitude and immediately memorialized. The congratulatory memorial stated: "His golden countenance and jade-like locks outshone the radiance of night’s luminaries. The white steed with its crimson mane left traces as wondrous as the celestial steeds’ birth." Recorded in the memorial of Court Gentleman for Ceremonials, Sun Rui.

Empress Wu Zetian of Zhou.

In the first year of Tisheng (684 CE), the jiashen year, the second month saw the era name changed to Wenming, and the ninth month to Guangzhai. After twenty-two years of regency, in the yisi year (705 CE), the era name was changed to Shenlong, lasting eighteen years in total.

In the first year of Wenming (684 CE), the jiashen year, Lao Jun descended upon Huangtian Plain in Haozhou, commanding Hao Yuanzong to convey to Empress Wu that she must not usurp the Mandate of Heaven. Recorded in the *Annals of Tang*.

In the fourth year of Jinglong (710 CE), the gengxu year, to resolve doubts during the pacification of internal strife, Lao Jun appeared as a white-robed elder selling divinations outside the Chunming Gate. His oracle read: "It is auspicious to seize the realm; the advantage lies within three days." Later, a temple was erected at the site. Recorded in *Strange Tales of Luozhong*.

**Emperor Xuanzong of Tang (Minghuang)**

In the first year of Kaiyuan (713 CE), the guichou year, twenty-nine years later, in the renwu year (742 CE), the era name was changed to Tianbao, and three years after that, in the jiashen year (744 CE), the term for the year was altered to *zai*.

In the seventeenth year of Kaiyuan (729 CE), Lao Jun descended upon Xinxing Temple in Shuzhou, his hidden radiance manifesting within a pillar of the Buddha hall, as vivid as if carved or painted—scrubbing and washing only made it clearer. Local civil and military officials, along with Daoists, monks, laypeople, and nuns, jointly memorialized the event, stating: "Appearing upon the hall’s pillar, its traces evoke the era of the historian’s craft. Dwelling within the Buddha’s shrine, it recalls the distant days of the *Huahu* transformation." Recorded in the memorial of Prefectural Governor of Yizhou, Zhang Jingzhong.

In the twenty-ninth year of Kaiyuan (741 CE), Lao Jun descended outside the Danfeng Gate, speaking to Tian Tongxiu: "Long ago, I entered the Flowing Sands and concealed a golden numinous talisman in Yin Xi’s former residence. Memorialize the Emperor to retrieve it." The Emperor dispatched envoys, who recovered it from the ruins of the Hangu Pass. Recorded in the *Annals of Tang*.

In the second year of Tianbao (743 CE), the guimao year, the first month, the Emperor bestowed upon Lao Jun the honorific *Great Sage Ancestor Mysterious Origin Emperor*. In the twelfth month, as the Emperor visited the Huaqing Palace, Lao Jun descended and appeared above the Chaoyuan Pavilion, prompting the Emperor to rename it the *Jiangsheng Pavilion* ("Pavilion of the Descended Sage"). Recorded in the *Annals of Tang*.

In the seventh year of Tianbao (748 CE), the wuzi year, the Emperor bestowed upon Lao Jun the honorific *Sage Ancestor Great Dao Mysterious Origin Emperor*. In the ninth year (750 CE), the gengyin year, Lao Jun descended upon Mount Taibai, telling the mountain dweller Wang Xuanyi that the Baoxian Grotto held a wondrous treasure and true talisman. The Emperor commanded Minister of Justice Wang Qi and others to seek it, and they indeed obtained it. Recorded in the *Annals of Tang*.

In the thirteenth year of Tianbao (754 CE), the jiayin year, on the guimao day of the second month, the Emperor performed sacrifices at the Taiqing Palace and added to Lao Jun’s honorific: *Great Sage Ancestor Supreme Great Dao Golden Portal Mysterious Heaven Origin Emperor*. Recorded in the *Annals of Tang*.

In the fifteenth year of Tianbao (756 CE), the bingshen year, as the Emperor fled to Shu, Lao Jun descended beside the Black Waters in Hanzhong Prefecture. The Emperor ordered a stone statue carved at the site of the apparition. Lao Jun also descended upon Changling in Lizhou, riding a white deer, foretelling the omen of reclaiming the mountains. An edict was issued to establish the Ziran Abbey at the site of the manifestation. Both events recorded in the *Annals of Tang*.

**Emperor Suzong**

In the fifteenth year of Tianbao (756 CE), the bingshen year, the reign title was changed to Zhide; three years later, in the wuyin year (758 CE), it was changed to Qianyuan; two years after that, in the gengzi year (760 CE), it was changed to Shangyuan.

In the second year of Zhide (757 CE), the dingyou year, Lord Lao descended upon Yunlong Cliff in Tonghua Prefecture, where earth met heaven and his majestic form shone resplendent. An edict was issued to depict his true likeness. The August Emperor composed a eulogy, which read:

*"By day he manifests as a pearl-like visage,
Floating in the void with auspicious radiance.
Daoists, Buddhists, and beings of heaven and earth
All bow in reverence and gaze in devotion.
We command the finest artistry be employed,
That all commanderies and states may behold."*

Recorded in the *Preface to the Auspicious Eulogies of the Supreme August Emperor*.

**Emperor Jingzong**
In the first year of Baoli (825 CE), the yisi year.

In the second year of Baoli (826 CE), the bingwu year, Lord Lao descended before the imperial path at the Taiqing Palace, revealing the location of a hidden pitfall in Chang’an County to Zheng Jian. Recorded in the stele inscription composed by Wei Chuhou and calligraphed by Liu Gongquan.

**Emperor Yizong**
In the first year of Xiantong (860 CE), the gengchen year.

In the tenth year of Xiantong (869 CE), the jichou year, Pang Xun led over three thousand men in an attempt to plunder the Taiqing Palace. At the time, several hundred officials and commoners had taken refuge within the palace. All witnessed Lord Lao traversing the sky, whereupon a sudden black mist descended, disorienting the rebels. They trampled one another in confusion, and Pang Xun drowned. Recorded in the memorial report of Li Wei, Military Commissioner of Bian Prefecture.

**Emperor Zhenzong of Song**

**Emperor Zhenzong of Song**
In the first year of Xiangfu (1008 CE), the wushen year.

In the seventh year of Dazhong Xiangfu (1014 CE), the jiayin year, the imperial carriage journeyed to Bozhou to pay homage at the Taiqing Palace. The emperor personally presented the imperial册宝, bestowing the august title *Supreme Lord Lao, the Primordial Emperor of Supreme Virtue*. Recorded in *Veritable Records of the Song Dynasty*.

**Emperor Huizong of Song**
In the first year of Zhenghe (1111 CE), the xinmao year.

In the second year of Zhenghe (1112 CE), the renchen year, Lord Lao, riding a white horse and borne upon auspicious clouds, descended to the Yuchen Temple on Mount Mao, where he transmitted to Liang Guangying the augmented *Scripture of the Heavenly Youth*. Other manifestations and apparitions unattached to specific eras are not recounted here. As for events such as radiant illuminations, auspicious omens, dream revelations, divine utterances, and miraculous validations—not involving the descent of an incarnate transformation—these too are recorded in the annals.

*Annals of the Primordial Sage, Scroll the First* concludes.

---
*Annals of the Primordial Sage, Scroll the Second*
Compiled by Gao Shi, Master of Observing the Return and Grand Daoist of the Song, Xie Shouyu.

The Most High Lord Lao is the ancestral founder of the Great Dao and the root origin of the Three Powers. Before the Supreme Ultimate, there was only vast emptiness—until the source of the Dao first stirred. The Dark Mother coalesced in primordial chaos, and from the murky depths emerged the first glimmer of embryonic radiance. Within it lay true essence, born of itself, which became spirit and illumination. By force of naming, it was called the Void Sovereign. Concealed, it governed the mysterious transformations; through the Dao’s movement, it ruled the world.

From the One Qi, the Three Qi emerged—these being the Mysterious, the Primordial, and the Origin. When the Three Qi blended, their subtle vapors gradually took form, giving rise to the beginnings of the ten thousand phenomena. None knew what came before, so it was forcibly named *Yuan* ("Origin"); none knew its beginning, so it was forcibly named *Shi* ("Commencement")—hence the title *Yuanshi Tianzun* ("Heavenly Worthy of Primordial Beginning"). As the Three Qi generated one another, the Nine Qi merged, giving birth to the various heavens and completing the worlds. None knew its greatness, so it was forcibly named *Tai* ("Supreme"); none knew its height, so it was forcibly named *Shang* ("Most High"). It stood foremost beyond the Ultimate, and gazing upward, it was called *Lao* ("Ancient"); governing without self, it was called *Jun* ("Lord")—thus was formed the title *Yuanshang Santian Xuanyuan Shi Sanqi Taishang Laojun* ("Most High Lord Lao of the Three Heavens of Primordial Origin, the Three Qi, and the Mysterious Beginning").

Initially, from the One Qi arose the Three Qi, which constitute the Three Heavens. The Three Qi combined to generate the Nine Qi, which constitute the Nine Heavens. From the Great Brahma Heaven descended the Three Pure Realms: the Heaven of Qingwei, the Heaven of Yuyu, and the Heaven of Dachi. Below the Three Heavens arose the nine great Brahma Heavens: Yudan Heaven, Shanshan Heaven, Xuyan Heaven, Douyan Heaven, Bujiaole Heaven, Dongyuan Heaven, Fanfu Heaven, Qingming Heaven, and Wuxiang Heaven. Each of the Nine Heavens further generated three heavens below, totaling thirty-six heavens. All lesser Brahma Heavens beyond these are subordinate to these great Brahma Heavens. The Nine Qi are the Fused Qi, the Blazing Qi, the Evolving Qi, the Vast Qi, the Radiant Qi, the Dao Qi, the Chaotic Qi, the Penetrating Qi, and the Boundless Qi.

Next are the Four Heavens of Seed-Peoples: the Heaven of Supreme Ultimate Peace and Nurturance, the Heaven of Dragon Transformation and Brahma Salvation, the Heaven of Jade Eminence and Ascendant Victory, and the Heaven of Great Emptiness and Constant Fusion. These are the Heavens of Seed-Peoples, also called the Seed-Humans, for at the beginning of each kalpa, they descend to become the progenitors of humanity. The Buddhists refer to them as the Four Dhyāna Heavens. Above, these heavens draw from the Three Thousand Three Hundred Million *xi* of the Three Pure Realms of the Great Clarity; below, they generate the Five Thousand Five Hundred Fifty-Five Million *xi* of the Eight Brahma Heavens. Each *xi* measures three thousand *li*. These heavens lie beyond the Three Realms, transcending the reckonings of yin and yang, and thus are not bound by limits of years or lifespans, nor can they be destroyed by the calamities of water, fire, or wind.

Next are the Three Realms: the Realm of Desire with its six heavens, the Realm of Form with its eighteen heavens, and the Formless Realm with its four heavens. Then come the Eight Brahma Heavens: Beginning Azure Heaven, Azure Origin Heaven, Beginning Cinnabar Heaven, Supreme Cinnabar Heaven, Beginning Plain Heaven, Supreme Plain Heaven, Beginning Mysterious Heaven, and Supreme Mysterious Heaven. Next is the human world, divided into eight directions: the Pure and Tranquil World of the North, the Everlasting Peace World of the Northeast, the Welcoming Virtue World of the East, the Employing Worthies World of the Southeast, the Abandoning Worthies World of the South, the Benevolent and Tranquil World of the Southwest, the Pure Conduct World of the West, and the Extending Worthies World of the Northwest. Below these lie the Nine Earths, which solidify into mountains and merge into seas and marshes.

The First Earth is the Moist and Lustrous Earth; the Second, the Hard and Lustrous Earth; the Third, the Unctuous and Lustrous Earth; the Fourth, the Moist Earth; the Fifth, the Golden Grain Earth; the Sixth, the Diamond and Iron Earth; the Seventh, the Water-Restrained Earth; the Eighth, the Great Wind Earth; and the Ninth, the Penetrating Spring and Colorless Net Earth. Each layer consists of one stratum of soil, one of water, and one of wind, descending from above.

The essence of yang becomes the sun; the essence of yin becomes the moon. The essences of the sun, moon, and Five Phases coalesce into the stars. When the Two Qi interact, the myriad beings of plants and animals mutually generate and transform. As the *Scripture on Establishing the Kalpas* states: "Within the formless and nameless, the turbid and chaotic, I opened the Mysterious Yellow of the Dao, divided the numinous, and dispersed the qi. From the Great Brahma Heaven descended the Three Realms; next arose the Nine Heavens. The Nine Emperors were established as the mysterious laws of the Three Treasures; the twenty-seven heavens became the cultivated realms of the boundaries. The thirty-six departments formed the mysterious roots of the Three Realms, and below, they became the domains of the thirty-six heavens. Next came the thirty-two heavens and thirty-two emperors, who subtly governed the transformations. Below, they divided into the Three Realms, laterally connecting to the revolving mechanism of the twenty-eight constellations. The Five Stars wove their paths to illuminate the five directions. The pure qi ascended; the heavy and turbid congealed below. Below arose the Nine Earths; in the middle arose the Nine Humans. Heaven, earth, and all beings were thus complete.

Thus, the harmonious and upright qi of yang gave birth to the lofty perfected sages; the gentle and tranquil qi of softness gave birth to the Primordial Ladies, sagely consorts, female immortals, and jade maidens; the fierce and valiant qi gave birth to the Heavenly Soldiers, the Divine Generals, and the martial officers; the qi of yin, yang, and the Five Phases gave birth to men and women; and the chaotic and errant qi gave birth to birds and beasts. All derive from the One Non-Being, yet their myriad forms differ according to their generation.

At the end of a great kalpa, from the Nine Earths up to the Formless Realm, the Three Calamities arise, and the ten thousand phenomena dissolve. Above the Heavens of Seed-Peoples, the calamities do not reach. The Primordial Qi recombines, returning to chaos. After the kalpa reopens, the heavenly beings are once more commanded to descend as human seed, becoming rulers and ministers. They propagate the great Dao and establish the laws, disseminating transformations in accordance with the times. Countless vast kalpas have passed, and all have proceeded thus.

As the *Scripture of Supreme Clarity* states: The heavens are round with twelve guiding principles; the earth is square with twelve governing mechanisms. The heavenly principles revolve through three hundred sixty degrees, forming the yang comet; the earthly mechanisms advance through three thousand six hundred degrees, forming the yin eclipse. The heavenly principles complete one revolution in three hundred thirty days; the earthly mechanisms advance one degree in three thousand three hundred days. Nine thousand nine hundred degrees mark the convergence of heaven and earth’s qi, known as the Great Yang Nine and the Great Hundred Six—also called the Great Kalpa and the Great Cycle. Multiplying these numbers, a minor yang comet occurs roughly once every three hundred thirty years, which constitutes the Lesser Yang Nine Calamity.

One hundred eighty-nine thousand years mark the completion of the heavenly principles’ revolution, thirty-three thousand cycles of the earthly mechanisms’ advancement, and the convergence of three thousand three hundred degrees of the Great Cycle. As heaven moves and earth remains still, yang is swift while yin is slow—hence the distinction between comets and eclipses. At this time, heavenly qi is exhausted in the Great Yin, and earthly qi reaches its peak in the Great Yang. When yang is at its extreme, comets appear; when yin is at its extreme, stagnation arises. At yang’s extremity, its essence transforms into water; at yin’s extremity, its essence transforms into fire. First, the world is consumed by great fire, then submerged by great floods—rising to the space beneath the Nine Heavens, descending to the depths within the Nine Earths—until gold and jade dissolve, and not even the smallest trace remains. Only then do the primordial qi recombine, known as the Primal Chaos. When the Primal Chaos divides again, the Three Heavens’ sages and the Four Heavens’ seed-people descend to teach and transform the world, just as at the beginning of this kalpa, when the Three Sovereigns and Five Emperors succeeded one another in governance. Such transformations are collectively called the Cycles of Convergence and Separation.

The Most Venerable Lord has endured these cycles of separation and convergence through countless kalpas, as the *Scripture of Western Ascension* states: *"Movement brings the burden of kalpas; I reflect on the toil and hardship."* This is what it means.

The *Comprehensive Records of Customs* states: *"Ten thousand days make a wan, ten wan make a yi, ten yi make a zhao, ten zhao make a jing, ten jing make a gai, and ten gai make a zai."* The term *zai* signifies that the earth can no longer bear it.

According to the *Nine Heavens’ Chapters on the Generation of Spirits*: When the Great Cycle nears its end and the count concludes on the year of *jiashen*, the Three Officials wield their brushes to assess and distinguish the seed-people, calculating merits and transgressions to separate the good from the evil. From the era of Red Clarity to the first year of the Supreme Sovereign, those who received initiation according to the *Primordial Yang Jade Treasury* numbered two hundred forty thousand. From the era of Kaihuang to the year of *jiashen*, as the heavens select the worthy, the offices of immortals lie vacant, and the celestial bureaucracy remains unfilled. According to the *Primordial Yang Jade Calendar*, three generations must pass before those of sincere heart, who accumulate goodness and establish merit, are recommended by the Three Realms and protected by the Five Emperors—those whose names are recorded in the heavens—are chosen, ten thousand in number, to fill these roles. An additional one hundred twenty thousand are to be selected as reserve officials. The Three Officials correspond in harmony, inscribing the names of the seed-people in reverse order, for they are destined to be born in the Four Heavens as the people of the next kalpa.

Furthermore, the Nine Dark Prisons receive the Nine Dragon Talismanic Mandate from the Azure Palace of the Eastern Marchmount, commanding the liberation of the male and female souls of the dead in the Nine Dark Prisons—those whose past lives bore good names, whose merits and virtues are complete, and who are destined to receive deliverance. Thirty-two thousand such souls are chosen to replenish the people of the Great Prosperity after the purgation of *jiashen*. All kalpas follow this pattern, with destinies scrutinized by the Most Venerable Lord.

The form of heaven and earth resembles that of a chicken’s egg, encircled by primordial darkness like the halo around the sun. Thus, there are five hundred five million five hundred fifty-five myriad layers of heaven and earth, each containing its own celestial patterns and terrestrial principles, circulating yin and yang and the Five Phases, arraying gods and spirits, generating the myriad things, wielding the handle of life and completion, and anchoring the origin of creation and transformation. Therefore, in the heavens, he is the most revered among all sages; in the world, he is the master of all teachings. He is called Laozi, the embodiment of the Dao. His manifestations are not singular, and his titles are boundless—sometimes thirty-six, sometimes seventy-two. He may be called the Supreme August Emperor of the Nine Heavens, the Sovereign of the Cavern-Realm and Primordial Unity, the Most High Jade Emperor, the Great Emperor of Longevity, the Marvelous Black August Lord of Supreme Peace and Perfect Authenticity, the Emperor of the Nine Mysteries, the Dharma King of the Great Thousand, the Elder of the Nine Numinous, the Left Mystic Perfected of the Supreme Clarity, the Great Dharma Master of the Three Caverns’ Wondrous Scriptures of the Golden Palace, the Most High Great Dharma King, the Mystic Unity of True Stillness and Light, the Latter Sage of the Golden Palace, the Lord of the Nine Elders’ Immortal Capital, the Nine-Black Elder, the Supreme Elder, the Lord of the Twelve Hundred Offices, the Supreme Scenery Lord of Supreme Peace, the Father of Non-Action, or the Mother of the Myriad Things.

At the time of his descent into the world, the divine beings of the ten directions reverently bear wisdom, the Most Honored, the Teacher of Emperors, the Great Man, the Venerable Immortal, the Father of Heaven and Humankind, the Supreme Person of Non-Action, the Great Compassionate One, the Benevolent, and the Master of the True Origin. The heavenly and earthly beings praise him with ten titles: the Lord of Non-Action, the Supreme Mystic Elder, the Most Venerable Lord Lao, the Most High Laozi, the Great Emperor of the Heavenly Sovereign, the Great Dharma Master of the Mystic Center, the Ancient Great Master, the Emperor of the Golden Palace, the Most High Supreme August, and the Great Perfected of Emptiness and Non-Being. He is also known by titles such as the Perfect and Boundless Great Dao, the Natural and Primordial Most High Heavenly Worthy, the Lord of the Dao, the Supreme Heavenly Perfected, the Heavenly Elder, the Heavenly Master, the Yellow Elder, the Mystic Ancestor, the Teacher of the World, the Divine Person, the Perfected, the Immortal, the Utmost Person, the Great Person, the Daoist, and the Sage. The titles from the Heavenly Perfected downward each consist of two characters.

The Most Venerable Lord, the Cavern-Realm’s Ultimate Sage, has no fixed form. When he dissolves, he becomes darkness; when he rests, he becomes human. At times, he coalesces into his true form within the Great Void, his body boundless, his features perfectly complete, with nothing above to grasp and nothing below to tread upon. At other times, he resides upon the Cloud Blossom, his body golden, attended by ten thousand perfected beings and revered by a hundred spirits. Or he sits within a lotus, wearing a crown adorned with the Seven Luminaries, draped in a nine-colored radiant robe, his neck bearing a halo that illuminates heaven and earth. Or he dwells in a jeweled hall and golden palace, surrounded by pearl and jade curtains, as ten thousand emperors pay homage and divine soldiers guard his carriage. Sometimes his form is golden and jade-like, clad in yellow garments and embroidered robes; at others, he wears plain robes and a dark cap, riding a white horse with a red mane. At times, he governs the Ten Heavens, sealing and overseeing the myriad people, residing in the Supreme Subtlety, the Curved Array, or the Purple Chamber as the Great Emperor of the Heavenly Sovereign. In spring, he transforms into the Supreme Scenery Lord, nine thousand *zhang* tall, wearing a crown of the Seven Treasures’ radiant flowers, dressed in robes of dark yellow and black, with a flying skirt of blue brocade, holding a tiger tally, and seated upon a seven-colored cloud.

In summer, he transforms into the Venerable Elder, wearing a crown of nine dragons, clad in robes of yellow patterns and a skirt of yellow feathers, holding a golden tablet, standing upon purple clouds. In autumn, he becomes a youth, dressed in five-colored garments, sometimes riding a lion, sometimes seated upon blue clouds. In winter, he manifests as a radiance of dark, mysterious, and azure hues, their luminous chaos intertwining—this is the return to the Black of the Golden Palace, where he further refines the essence of soaring mystery and dawn’s communion.

At times, he incarnates as the Great Emperor of the Dark Heavens. The scriptures say that in eighty-two transformations he becomes True Martial. Thus, the Invocation of the Protector Sage Perfected Lord declares: *"We reverently invoke the Great Sage of the Dark Heavens, the numinous spirit of the northern *ren* and *gui*, the True Honored One of the Golden Palace who manifests in response, the Supreme General known as True Martial."* His divine potency is self-sufficient; he appears as he is perceived. He can be white or black, square or round, bent or extended, long or short, old or young, one or ten thousand. His form shifts and reverses without constancy.

At times, he is the Twelve Hundred Elders, manifesting across the heavens. At others, he is the One Hundred Eighty Dao Lords, guiding the mortal world, dispersing his numinous radiance in fleeting, boundless presence—yet the essence of his True One remains serene and eternally quiescent, ever abiding in the Grand Clarity and the Palace of the Supreme Ultimate.

Once, in the first year of *Shanghe*—the year *gengyin* of the celestial reckoning, on the ninth day of the ninth month, the *jiazi* day—Lord Lao was born within the Jade Country of the Northern *Yudan* realm, at the Valley of Li between the Heavenly Mirror Mountain. His mother, the Mysterious Numinous Mother of the Nine Mysteries’ Chamber, first conceived him in a dream where dark clouds, sun, and moon entwined her form, and the lightning of the Six Qi stirred her spirit, thus quickening with child. On the day of his birth, three suns rose together, and so he took the valley as his clan name and the radiant light as his given name. He was also called *Hong*, styled *Ziguang*; another name was *Xuanshui*, styled *Shanyuan*.

*Shanghe* is but one of the celestial eras, akin to *Chiming*, *Zhuling*, *Qinghan*, *Tianhan*, *Kaihuang*, and *Shanghuang*. Yet worldly scholars, knowing only that the *jiazi* cycle was devised by *Danao* and that reign titles began with Emperor Wu of Han, dismiss such celestial eras as fabrications. Little do they realize that the heavens have recorded years since countless kalpas past, though mortals remain unaware.

From *Guiguzi* to *Beiguozi*, from Celestial Master Zhang to *Ge Xian’gong*, all have drawn upon celestial era names to align with mortal ages. Otherwise, how could these immortals, versed in ancient and modern lore, delving into the profound and subtle, be ignorant that reign titles did not exist before Qin and Han? From the dawn of creation, when laws and institutions were established, to the rise and fall of dynasties, all is predestined by heaven, which dispatches celestial perfected beings to transmit teachings to the mortal world—not by mortal hands could such be devised beforehand. Let scholars ponder this.

Thereupon, he gathered his hun souls and refined his po spirits, guarded the womb’s treasured spirit, recorded his essence and stabilized his blood, solidified his fluids and strengthened his sinews. He swallowed light and drank mist, chewed the roots of flight, his inner virtue perfectly full, his external burdens far severed. His forms multiplied into millions, his transformations boundless.

The Supreme Perfected Lord of the Purple Tenuity and the Jade Clarity Heavenly Emperor dispatched an eight-scene jade chariot to welcome him, ascending to the Palace of Supreme Clarity. There, he was bestowed the *Ruigang* Elixir and the Jade Phoenix Seal, the Golden Perfection and Jade Radiance, the talismans of the Divine Tiger and the feathers of flight, a crimson brocade dragon skirt, a blue mantle with tiger belt, and the Crown of Round Countenance. He received the scriptures and was named the Posterior Sage Emperor Lord of the Golden Palace.

In the first year of *Longhan*, Lord Lao divided his body in the Central Land of Great Blessing, revealing the True Writ of Red Script to transform its people, who all attained longevity. Later, in the Southern Culmen’s *Chiming* Land, he issued the Fire-Refined True Writ, thus naming it the Court of Cavernous Yang, where a Pool of Flowing Fire exists. Those who refined their forms therein became golden in hue. Above, he established the Palace of Southern Prosperity; below, the Lodge of Vermilion Mound, to govern generation and completion.

Across the five kalpas of *Longhan*, *Chiming*, *Shanghuang*, *Yankang*, and *Kaihuang*, Lord Lao cyclically wielded the qi of *Beginning Green*, *Cinnabar Radiance*, *Central Numinosity*, *Pristine Florescence*, and *Mysterious Yang*, revolving them into the Jade Calendar. Since *Longhan*, through boundless kalpas, within the vastness of primordial chaos where no light shone, records could not be traced. Only with the *Chiming* Unfolding Chart did scriptures become discernible.

The True Writ is the essence of the Five Directions’ true qi, congealed into script, its eight corners trailing rays. It may take the form of cloud-seal characters or assume the shapes of flight and movement—these are the talismanic writs of today, the covenants of celestial perfected beings. The above is found interspersed within the Three Caverns’ true scriptures.

Moreover, in the Eastern Culmen’s *Biluo* Heaven, within the *Fuli* Land, he inscribed the True Writ upon the Azure Forest, forming characters of purple hue. The wind through its trees produced music, and birds that ate its leaves grew patterned plumage. Those who obtained its feathers could fly. Its people lived long, at peace and without striving.

In the Western Culmen’s *Weiluo* World, within the *Xinayu* Land, he issued the True Writ upon the *Fuluo* Peaks to deliver its people. Jade pools arose spontaneously, golden essence flowed and shimmered; those who ladled its waters grew golden radiance, becoming equal to heaven.

In the Northern Land of *Yudan*, he inscribed the True Writ within the Cavernous Numinosity Abbey to deliver its multitudes. Below lay the Cold Pool’s numinous springs, naturally flowing and abundant; those who drank thereof knew no end.

Within these five lands, all received Lord Lao’s teachings of the Numinous Treasure, attaining longevity. Thus, he commanded the Five Elder Thearchs to guard the Five Directions, propagating the Dao and extending teachings to harmonize and pacify all beings.

The *History of the Sui Dynasty: Treatise on Classics and Books* states: *"The Celestial Worthy of Primordial Beginning was born before the Great Nonbeing, inheriting the qi of spontaneity. Profound and distant, none know his limits. Though heaven and earth collapse and kalpas end, the body of the Celestial Worthy remains eternally indestructible."*

Each time heaven and earth first unfold, whether upon the Jade Capital above or in the wilds of Qiongsang, he imparts the secret Dao, calling it "Opening the Kalpa to Deliver Humankind." Yet this opening of the kalpa has occurred not once but many times, hence the era names: Yankang, Chiming, Longhan, and Kaihuang. The scriptures he expounds are likewise endowed with the qi of Primordial Unity, existing spontaneously and not by fabrication, just as the Celestial Worthy abides eternally undiminished. While heaven and earth remain unbroken, these texts lie concealed and untransmitted; when the kalpic cycle unfolds, their words appear of themselves. He then commands the Heavenly Perfected Sovereign to transform and elucidate the celestial sounds, and from the Heavenly Perfected down to the various immortals, they transmit them in turn through successive ranks. Only when the immortals receive them do they begin to bestow them upon the world. In their great purport, these teachings ultimately return to benevolence, love, and purity; through accumulation and cultivation, one gradually attains longevity, naturally undergoing spiritual transformation, ascending to immortality in broad daylight, and merging one’s body with the Dao.

The *Daode Jing* of Zhang Shangying of the Song states: "The kalpic cycles stretch vast and boundless, the Great and Lesser [Dao] obstructed and blocked; heterodox flourishing loses the Primordial, scattering and manifesting among the multitudes. Through their nine orifices, emotions and perceptions arise. As emotions flow and perceptions obscure, one becomes entangled and inverted. From this flow arises attachment, and from obscuration arises aversion. Aversion and attachment assail one another, rising and falling in succession; abandoning clarity for darkness, the accumulation of darkness forms yin. Yin congeals into obscurity, and entering obscurity, one becomes a ghost. When the spirit is upright, one takes human form; when deviant, one enters other destinies—devouring, oppressing, their natures unable to attain stillness, their lives unable to endure. Dark flourishing and gloomy miasma offend the celestial extremes. The Three Clarities’ transforming lords, the Three Thearchs and Celestial Lords, observing from above, a single thought arouses compassion. Spontaneous wondrous flourishing weaves into patterns; a numinous wind stirs and plays, forming sounds of its own. Utmost compassion delivers from distress; utmost benevolence cherishes life; utmost rectitude crushes the heterodox; utmost clarity shatters darkness. Above, celestial offices are arrayed; below, mountain grottoes are established. The host of perfected beings receive their duties; the ranked immortals divide their governance. Once the true mechanism is revealed, the jade script emerges. Fire refines the Cavernous Yang; brushes inscribe the Azure Void. Jade seals and golden tablets, talismans and oral incantations are taught to the immortal throng, wielding authority to restrain demonic hordes, refining and delivering souls and spirits, commanding the myriad numina.

The Supreme Dao of the Most High has three [methods]; the Dao of the Upper Perfected has seven; the Dao of the Middle Perfected has six; the Dao of the Lower Perfected has four. What the Golden Mouth has spoken, what the Three Masters have transmitted—precious jade caskets and sacred bamboo tubes—are secretly stored on Mount Tiantai. Those that have fallen among humankind, a single tablet from the Great Granary, are collected by cultivators of the true into the Three Caverns. The utterly non-existent Upper Perfected are called the Cavern of the True. The profound, subtle, and wondrous are called the Cavern of the Mysterious. The numinous, marvelous, hidden, and manifest are called the Cavern of the Numinous. That which is true beyond the true dissolves into quiescence without pattern. That which is primordial beyond the primordial abides in wondrous solitude. That which is numinous beyond the numinous is revered and boundless. Such is the purport of the true texts of the Three Caverns.

Lord Lao further transformed his body, styling himself the Celestial Worthy of Tranquil Aging. He propagated his teachings across the Five Directions, then on the Ninefold Mystic Terrace of Mount Donghua expounded the Dao to the King of the Eastern Ultimate and Primordial Elder. The king’s consort, princes, and ministers—over five thousand in all—together cultivated this Dao and all attained earthly immortality. Thereupon, they established the Abbey of Immortal Practice, the Sevenfold Upright and Twofold Mystic Halls, where aspiring immortals resided. Within two hundred years, over three thousand in the land ascended to heaven in broad daylight, and the king ascended to become the Lord of the Wondrous Brahmā Heaven.

According to the *Inner Writ of the Azure Lad*: "The Land of the Primordial Elder lies beyond the Eastern Sea; it is also called the Land of Pure Harmony, where the Lord of the Wondrous Brahmā Heaven resides. Later, due to excessive indulgence in pleasure, he was demoted to the human realm as the king of Jibin, whom Laozi transformed into the Buddha." During the era of the Heavenly Thearch, Lord Lao was known as the Great Master of the Mystic Center, also called the Celestial Master of Penetrating the Mysterious. He revealed the *Twelve Books of the Cavern of the True*, teaching the Great Dao of the Non-Ultimate to the human realm. During the era of the Earthly Thearch, he was known as the Ancient Great Master, revealing the *Twelve Books of the Cavern of the Mysterious* and transforming humankind with the Dao of the Supreme and Perfectly True. During the era of the Human Thearch, he was known as Master Pangu, revealing the *Twelve Books of the Cavern of the Numinous* and transforming humankind with the Dao of Grand Peace and Non-Action.

During the time of Fuxi, he descended to the fields, styling himself Yuhua Zi, bestowing the *Inner Writ of the Heavenly Thearch* and the *River Chart* of the Eight Trigrams, teaching humankind the Dao of aligning with one’s nature. During the time of Zhu Rong, he descended to Mount Heng, styling himself Guangshou Zi, bestowing the *Inner Writ of the Human Thearch* and teaching the Dao of pacifying the spirit, enabling the molding of clay into vessels to transform raw and cooked. During the time of Shennong, he descended to Jiyin, styling himself Dacheng Zi, bestowing the *Inner Writ of the Earthly Thearch* and teaching the Dao of cherishing life, enabling the sowing of grains and fruits to replace cooking and killing, and the harmonizing of medicinal recipes to cure illness and nurture one’s nature. These events are briefly recorded in the Tang annals.

During the time of the Yellow Thearch, he descended to Mount Kongtong, styling himself Guangcheng Zi. In the twenty-ninth year of his reign, the Yellow Thearch, troubled that the world was not well-governed, went to see Guangcheng Zi and asked: "I have heard that you have attained the Ultimate Dao. I wish to draw upon the essence of heaven and earth to aid the five grains and nourish the people, and to observe yin and yang to fulfill the needs of all living beings. How may this be done?" Guangcheng Zi replied: "What you inquire about is the substance of things; what you desire to manage is the destruction of things. Since you began governing the world, the clouds and rain no longer gather before falling, the grasses and trees no longer wait to yellow before falling, and the light of the sun and moon has grown dim. As for those glib-tongued flatterers of yours, how could they be worthy of speaking of the Ultimate Dao?"

The Yellow Thearch withdrew, relinquished the world, built a solitary chamber, spread a mat of white cogon grass, and advanced on his knees with the wind at his back. Bowing twice, he prostrated himself and asked: "I have heard that you, Master, have attained the Ultimate Dao. I venture to ask: how may one govern the body so as to attain longevity?" Guangcheng Zi rose with a frown and said: "Excellent question! Come, and I shall tell you."

The essence of the Ultimate Dao is profound and obscure, its apex dim and silent. See nothing, hear nothing, embrace the spirit in stillness—then the body will naturally align. Be pure, be still; do not weary your form, do not disturb your essence. Reduce thought, curb desire, and you may attain long life. Let the eyes see nothing, the ears hear nothing, the heart know nothing—then the spirit will guard the body, and the body will endure. Guard your inner self, close off the outer; excessive knowledge leads to ruin.

I have guided you to the source of supreme yang, the radiance of great clarity. I have led you through the gate of profound obscurity, the source of supreme yin. Heaven and earth have their offices, yin and yang their treasuries. Guard your body with care, and all things will flourish of themselves. I preserve the One and dwell in harmony. Thus I have cultivated my body for one thousand two hundred years, yet my form has never declined.

The Yellow Thearch bowed twice and prostrated himself, saying: "Master, you speak as heaven itself."

Guangcheng Zi then said to the Yellow Thearch: "Come, I shall tell you more. Those things are infinite, yet the people all deem them finite. Those things are unfathomable, yet all take them as limits. Those who attain my Dao become emperors above and kings below. Those who lose my Dao see light above yet become earth below. Now, all the myriad beings are born from the earth and return to the earth. Therefore, I shall depart from you, entering the gate of the infinite to wander the boundless wilds. I share the light of the sun and moon, and endure with heaven and earth."

Thereupon, he bestowed upon the Thearch the *Scripture of the Hidden Talisman*. In the era of the Three Sovereigns, the Old Lord expounded the scriptures, which the world called the *Three Tombs*—long lost to transmission. The scriptures taught across generations were often concealed in jade chambers and jasper terraces, or secreted in the Dragon Palace’s sea vaults, guarded by divine immortals, unknown to the world. What has been transmitted is but a single filament from Mount Tai.

Later, the Queen Mother of the West was commanded to present the Thearch with the jade image of the Primordial Celestial Worthy. The Thearch placed it in a lofty observatory, reverently enshrining it, where it was ever veiled by colored clouds—hence the name "Daoist abbey." The term "Daoist abbey" began here.

According to the *Extensive Records of the Taiping Era*, as cited in the Daoist scriptures: In ancient times, the Dao was dark and quiescent, its essence formless and inactive. When it wished to initiate mysterious workings and transform the myriad things, it first generated the Lord of the East through the radiance of the Eastern Flower’s perfect yang. Born upon the Azure Sea in the wastes of the Blue Spirit, he presided over the warmth of yang and governed the eastern realm, known as the Lord of the East. Then, through the mystery of the Western Flower’s perfect yin, it generated the Queen Mother, who oversaw the origin of life, her divine profundity concealed in the vastness. She distilled the pure essence of the Great Dao, condensing its radiance into form, and together with the Lord of the East, they governed the two qi, nurturing heaven and earth, shaping the myriad things. Embodying the root of soft compliance, she was the primal yin, her position matched to the west, mothering all beings—hence the name Queen Mother of the West. In heaven above, on earth below, across the three realms and ten directions, all women who ascend as immortals and attain the Dao are subject to her.

The Lord of the East wears the Triple-Support Crown and robes of nine-colored cloud and mist. He is also called the Jade Sovereign Lord, dwelling in the Cloud Chamber, his canopy of purple cloud, his city of blue cloud. Immortal youths stand in attendance, jade maidens scatter incense, and countless divine officials and immortals serve in their offices. Thus, all men who attain the Dao have their names recorded under his registry. He visits the Nine-Spirit Metal Mother twice yearly, touring her palace to jointly assess and rank the merits of male and female immortals, promoting or demoting them by their deeds. Through the cycles of heaven and earth, the alternation of yin and yang, the rise and fall of time, the calamities of yang-nine and yin-six, the exaltation of the good and demotion of the wicked—all proceed by their decree. They compile the registers and submit them to the Primordial Celestial Worthy, who transmits them through the Jade Dawn to the Old Lord, who in turn bestowed the Dao upon the Yellow Thearch. Thus, the Metal Mother was commanded to reveal the image of the Primordial Celestial Worthy.

The Old Lord further commanded the Thearch to ascend Mount Wangwu, open the stone coffer, and retrieve the jade writ, obtaining the Way of the Nine Cauldrons’ divine elixir and the furnace fire of flying snow. The Thearch then cast the cauldrons at Mount Jing, refined the elixir, and consumed it. Clouds and dragons came to welcome him, and he ascended on a dragon. Seventy-two of his ministers and attendants likewise ascended with him. The lesser officials, unable to follow, grasped the dragon’s whiskers and clung to the Thearch’s bow and cauldron, falling as they wailed. The world called this the "Crow-Caw Bow." The people, unable to follow, took his relics to Mount Ba and built a tomb to enshrine them, naming it Mount Ba. They also buried his robes and cap at Mount Qiao, calling it the Yellow Thearch’s Mausoleum. Where the cauldron fell was named Cauldron Lake. Today, atop Mount Xiandu in Jinyun County of Chuzhou, there is a Cauldron Lake, inaccessible by path, where golden lotuses grow. Their leaves often drift down to the Twin Streams, hence the name Jinhua County. Anciently, the Thearch’s clan was called Jinyun, so the county was named thus—truly not in vain.

Initially, the Old Lord descended to the world to establish teachings, revealing the secrets of cultivation and the standards of master-disciple transmission. In the first year of the Upper Sovereign’s reign, on the seventh day of the seventh month, he journeyed to the Western River. There, he beheld the Primordial Celestial Worthy riding an Eight-Scenery Jade Chariot, drawn by nine-colored dark dragons, with three pure flying clouds, leading a procession of immortals, floating through the void to meet him above the Western River. The Celestial Worthy exhaled the Jade Talisman of the Cavernous Mystery’s Inner Vision, bestowing it upon the Old Lord. The Old Lord bowed deeply, received the teaching, and ingested the talisman. Within his body, the eight luminous spirits of the three divisions appeared, and twenty-four diagrams of golden script and jade characters shone forth in the void, illuminating all without limit, their patterns naturally unfolding. He commanded the immortal in charge of the diagrams to transcribe them—golden script in purple characters, cinnabar slips and jade tablets—thus establishing them. All the true texts bestowed by the Supreme Perfected Lady of the Nine Lights of the Upper Prime of the Southern Culmen, the Eastern and Western Flowers, the Northern and Southern Perfected Lords, the immortals of the Five Peaks, and the Pure Void Perfected Ones—all originated from the Old Lord.

The diagrams are divided into three ranks: upper, middle, and lower.

**Upper Rank:**
1. *Diagram of the Divine Immortals’ Bathing in the Eastern Well*
2. *True Forms of the Five Peaks*
3. *Eight Histories of the Essence of the Communicative Spirit*
4. *Diagram of the Six Jia’s Spiritual Communication*
5. *Diagram of the Nine Palaces and Purple Chambers*
6. *Diagram of the Primordial Beginning and Great Clarity*
7. *Diagram of the Perfected Dao’s Primal Unity*
8. *Diagram of the Western Ascent’s Preservation and Record*

**Middle Rank:**
1. *Diagram of the Divine Immortals’ Penetration of the Subtle and Spiritual Transformations*
2. *Diagram of Treading the Void and Ninefold Numinosity*
3. *Diagram of the Ninefold Transformations of Heaven*
4. *Diagram of Constant Preservation*
5. *Diagram of Guarding the One and Nurturing the Body*
6. *Diagram of Guarding the Spirit and Embracing the Radiance*
7. *Diagram of Silent Repose, Nurturing the True, and Guarding the Will*
8. *Diagram of the Lingzhi Mushroom and Jade Maidens*

**Lower Rank:**
1. *Diagram of the Six Yin Jade Maidens of the Divine Immortals*
2. *Diagram of the Nine-Nines Dao Immortals*
3. *Diagram of Daoist Exercises*
4. *Diagram of Vast Preservation in the Grotto*
5. *Diagram of Transformations and Hidden Prognostication*
6. *Diagram of Gathering Lingzhi and Opening the Mountains*
7. *Diagram of the Luminous Mirror*
8. *Diagram of the Limitless and Great Unity*

All twenty-four diagrams are arts of cultivating the body and attaining longevity, all perfected through the transformations of the Grotto Mystery and Primordial Beginning.

The Old Lord further oversaw the *Jade Dawn Divine Tiger Talisman Diagram* and the *Wisdom Plain Sutra*. All talismanic jade chapters of the *Highest Clarity Great Grotto True Scripture* for summoning numinous spirits and subduing demons were under his stewardship. These scriptures were all formed from the naturally coalescing pneumas of soaring mystery, their Dao lofty and wondrous, the most revered among all scriptures, governing the myriad spirits, guiding and ruling the host of immortals. They were concealed in the Palace of Great Abundance above the Nine Heavens, inscribed on golden slips to compile the numinous texts, and carved on cinnabar-inscribed jade to clarify their passages. Some were stored within the Jade Chamber of the Numinous Capital’s Jeweled Palace, guarded by great beasts, and protected by seven thousand poisonous dragons, divine tigers, and numinous spirits stationed at the Jade Tower. Three thousand Golden Dawn Jade Lads and Plain Numinous Jade Maidens each attended and safeguarded the sacred texts. The assembled Perfected Ones held banquets in ritual observance, and the ten thousand sages paid homage in audience.

The Jade Dawn Great Dao Lord often said to the Old Lord: “At the turning of the great kalpa, the teaching is bestowed upon the most worthy. If none are found, it remains untransmitted for kalpas. Later students seeking immortality, not knowing the origin of the Dao, vainly exhaust their thoughts in preservation, wearing out body and spirit. To seek the root, one must return to the source; losing the source while seeking life, none attain wholeness. The Jade Texts of the Highest Sovereign are transmitted only to those chosen; their methods are treasures, profoundly secret, beyond words. One must follow the luminous statutes and receive them in reverence.”

In the first year of the Middle Sovereign’s reign, on the first day of the third month of the renxu year, the Old Lord, in the Jeweled Chamber of the Jade Heaven, examined and collated the original sources, compiling the numinous chapters into three hundred volumes of sacred scriptures, seven thousand chapters of talismanic diagrams, and nine thousand jade instructions. He bestowed these upon the Azure Lad Great Lord of the Eastern Sea’s Fangzhu Palace, commanding their transmission to later students whose jade names matched the Perfected.

After receiving the sacred scriptures, the Great Lord ascended to the rank of High Minister. Three thousand Golden Flower Jade Maidens and Purple Dawn Jade Lads all attended and guarded him. Wielding the banner of the numinous talisman, he commanded demonic spirits, roamed the Purple Void’s halls, wandered the Azure Flower’s chambers, extinguished the Six Heavens at the end of the kalpa, and eradicated the myriad spirits in the mountains. He gathered later students from golden slips, collated the Azure Records in Fangzhu, extended the ten thousand emperors’ sojourn in the curved chambers, praised the sacred instructions in the wondrous chapters, compiled the independent in equal Perfection, and strictly governed the Four Poles to regulate the kalpa. Universally ruling the Nine Heavens and Nine Earths, the Five Peaks and famous mountains, the billions of Perfected Ones—none were not subject to him. The registers of life and death, even the minutest details, were all under his purview.

Later students wishing to receive the scriptures and cultivate the Dao must first submit golden slips to the Azure Palace, present jade tablets to the Highest Clarity, and be recorded by the Jade Bureau. The Dark Bureau constantly examines people’s essence and vigor; only those who are diligent and steadfast may receive the mysterious transmission.

The Old Lord further transmitted the teachings to the Great Void Perfected One, the Red Lord of the Southern Peak, commanding him to bestow them upon those who, having cultivated the Dao in past lives, bore golden names and jade characters, their names inscribed in the high pavilions, destined to become Perfected Ones. He also transmitted them to the Heavenly Perfected Sovereign and the Great Perfected Lady Wang. Some were sealed within the Western Mystery’s Wangwu Mountain, others carved upon the golden pillars and jade walls of the northern chamber of Penglai’s mansion. He also used five-colored jade slips, each sealed within the stone bamboo shoots of the Five Peaks. When the renchen year arrives to announce the assembly, the Later Sage Lord will descend, retrieve them, and entrust them to the Four Assistants, who will teach the worthy among the Highest Perfected.

According to the *Arrayed Records of the Later Sage Lord Li*: the Later Sage Lord Li’s Four Assistants and High Ministers—the Azure Lad Great Lord of Fangzhu Palace, the High Guardian of the Great Cinnabar Palace and Southern Culmen Primordial Lord, the High Tutor of the White Mountain Palace and Great Plain Perfected Lord, and the High Minister of the Western City Palace and Governor of All Perfected Lords—all sought immortality by pursuing these texts, grasping their fundamental origins, and thus attaining the Dao. Those who do not know the source of the Dao or the origin of the sacred instructions grope in darkness, their learning lacking a foundation. The Perfected will not descend, and the Dao will not manifest.

The Old Lord said: “The Three Caverns’ sacred scriptures are all the Upper Dao of the Three Clarities. I once received them from the Primordial Beginning Heavenly Worthy. For seven hundred million kalpas, as heaven and earth formed and dissolved, and the myriad beings arose and perished, only my Dao endured. Even now, I cultivate them above the Auspicious Clouds, regularly bestowing the Jade Clarity’s mysterious slips upon the Perfected Lords, and in the Heaven of Immeasurable Life, upon the Azure Lad Great Lord of Fangzhu. According to the Nine Heavens’ hierarchical standards, they emerge once every ten thousand kalpas. Since the beginning of the Kaihuang era, they have been transmitted to later students destined to become Perfected. Every nine thousand years, three may receive them; or within forty-nine years, if the right person appears, they may be transmitted all at once. Those who wish to receive my scriptures must follow the *Luminous Statutes of the Four Poles*, present precious offerings to their master, receive them to wear upon the body, and cultivate with a closed mind. Beware of careless transmission.”

According to the scriptural statutes governing the transmission of scriptures, the time limits vary. In high antiquity, when simplicity and harmony prevailed, they emerged but once in ten thousand kalpas. In this degenerate age, salvation is all the more urgent, and thus they may be transmitted upon encountering the right person within forty-nine years. All must prioritize purification through fasting and devote themselves to hidden merit, thereby redeeming the sins of the nine generations of ancestors, delivering all beings from suffering, and ultimately securing their own salvation. By establishing merit and spreading virtue, they uphold the celestial decrees and aspire to transcendence. Hence, there are twenty-seven grades of purification rites and thirty-six grades of jiao rituals. The highest employ clarity, emptiness, simplicity, and quiescence; the intermediate employ exhalation, inhalation, and the ingestion of qi; the lowest take the cleansing of the heart and repentance of transgressions as their foundation. Universally, they regard placing others before oneself as essential. With three thousand merits of practice, one ascends to heaven in broad daylight—this is attested.

It is further said: Those who wish to cultivate the supreme methods should first perform the Highest Cavern-Real Three Primordials Purification Rite. When the Three Primordials unite with the Real, they correspond above to the nine generations of ancestors. Those who wish to cultivate the *Thirty-Nine Chapters of the Great Cavern-Real Scripture*, the *Feminine One Jade Tablet of the Five Venerable Treasure Scripture*, the *Eighty-Two Supreme Vows of the Mysterious Mother*, or to wear the Divine Tiger and Golden Tiger Talismans, wield the Seven Radiant Flowing Gold Fire Bells to dissolve demons and conceal incantations, command

Lord Lao further transmitted to the Great Lord of the Azure Youth the *Numinous Writ of the Purple Text: Twenty-Four Practices of Cultivation*. Its summary states:

First is the method of gathering and ingesting flying roots and swallowing the qi of the sun. Begin by ingesting the *Luminous Opening Talisman*, constantly contemplating the moment of sunrise. Knock the teeth, silently intone the names of the sun’s essence and the characters of the Five Emperors within the sun. Visualize the five-colored streaming clouds from the sun approaching and enveloping the body, then inhale and swallow according to the method. One will feel the body suffused with jade-like luster and the face radiant with flowing light.

Next is the method of gathering and ingesting yin blossoms and swallowing the essence of the moon. Begin by ingesting the *Great Mystery Yin-Generation Talisman*, constantly contemplating the moment of moonrise. Knock the teeth, silently intone the names of the moon’s spirit and the characters of the Five Ladies within the moon. Visualize the five-colored crystalline radiance from the moon approaching and enveloping the body, then inhale and swallow according to the method. One will feel the body suffused with jade-like brilliance and the eyes alight with flying essence.

Next is the restraint of the three hun-souls. When the three hun-souls abandon the body to wander freely, swiftly departing to their original chamber, they may be detained by other spirits or captured by spectral entities. One must restrain and retain them to prevent their escape. The method involves constantly visualizing within the heart a great, revolving sphere of red and black that envelops the body, transforming into fire to illuminate the interior and exterior. Knock the teeth and intone the breath according to the method, and the three hun-souls will be restrained.

Next is the control of the seven po-souls. When the seven po-souls drift and wander through defiled and turbid realms, consorting with blood offerings, associating with ghosts and specters, clinging to corpses, or speaking of others’ transgressions and desiring their downfall—these are the afflictions of the po-souls. The method is practiced on the dark and new moons, the crescent and full moons, and the gengshen days. Visualize at the tip of the nose a gradually expanding sphere of white and black that crowns the body in nine layers, then transforms into the Four Numinous Beasts encircling the body. Intone the breath according to the method, and the seven po-souls will be refined and controlled.

Moreover, within the human body are the Three Primordial Palaces: the Upper Primordial Cinnabar Field, the Mud-Pill Palace, whose spirit is the Red Child, named Yuanxian, also called the Imperial Homeland; the Middle Primordial Cinnabar Field, the Crimson Palace, whose spirit is the Perfected One, named Zidan, also called Radiant Firmness; and the Lower Primordial Cinnabar Field, the Gate of Destiny Palace, whose spirit is the Infant, named Yuanyang, also called the Mysterious Valley. These Three Ones—clad in purple, red, and yellow robes respectively, each appearing as an infant—must be silently invoked by name and visualized in their proper attire and order when restraining the hun and po-souls.

Within the Gate of Destiny Palace resides the Great Lord, named Taokang, styled Heyan, who wears vermilion robes and a hibiscus crown, with the three hun-souls attending at his side. At night, before sleep, constantly visualize the Great Lord and invoke his guardianship according to the method for eighteen years. The Great Lord can stir the Three Fields on the left and govern the Three Blacks on the right, summoning the Yang Six Jia and the Yin Six Ding to attend the practitioner.

Furthermore, practice the *Way of Yu Yi and Jie Lin Rushing Toward Dawn*, ingest the *Numinous Flying Six Jia Yin-Yang Talismans*, wear the *Divine Tiger and Golden Tiger Demon-Dissolving Talismans of the Falling Flowing Gold*, recite the *True Scripture of the Great Cavern*, visualize the twenty-four spirits of the Three Sections and Eight Sceneries, ingest the *Jade-Tooth Flower Elixir*, embrace the *Yellow Water Moon Essence*, and consume the *Jade Essence of the Revolving Water and Ring of Hardness*. Then, seven-colored halos will emanate from the head, and one will achieve bodily transformation, commanding a thousand chariots and ten thousand riders to ascend to heaven in broad daylight.

These are the essential texts of Daoist cultivation, orally transmitted secrets from the Jade Clarity Lord, the Celestial Emperor of the Purple Tenuity and the Supreme Perfected of the Grand Tenuity, inscribed on purple jade tablets with azure-gold characters, with the Turtle Mother wielding the brush, the Golden Youth sweeping the mat, the Celestial Consort attending to incense, and the Jade Youth composing the text. It is titled the *Numinous Writ of the Purple Text* and was bestowed upon the Prime Minister, the Great Lord of the Azure Youth, to transmit to those in the Mysterious Palace whose jade names mark them as Perfected Ones. Thereupon, the Great Lord of the Azure Youth purified himself for a thousand days, prostrated himself on hands and knees, bowed his head to the north, and, following the ritual statutes, swore the covenant before returning to the Palace of the Square Cauldron in the Empyrean.

Later, it was transmitted to the Lord of Western City, who bestowed it upon those of auspicious bone-configuration. According to the scriptures: When the Great Veil of Heaven first unfolded its myriad patterns to gather and nurture the beings of the ten directions, it first established the Nine Sages, each divided into nine ranks. From the lowest to the immortal, there are eighty-one grades, for the Three Realms were shrouded in confusion and darkness. Thus, the Three Vehicles were established as paths of cultivation, differing in the superior, middle, and inferior, universally guiding all to awakening.

In the primordial era of Dragon Han, the sagely Dao was transmitted to the Venerable of the Nine Heavens and the Perfected Sovereign of the Nine Heavens. In the era of Red Clarity, it was transmitted to the Jade Emperor of the Void Sovereign. In the era of the Supreme Sovereign, the immortal Dao was transmitted to the Firstborn of the Myriad and the Jade Sovereign of the Great Perfected. These were the transmissions of the supreme sages.

In the era of Grand Simplicity, the virtue was bestowed upon the Grand Lord of the Supreme. In the era of Grand Beginning, it was bestowed upon the Celestial Emperor. In the era of Grand Origin, it was bestowed upon the Celestial Emperor of the Grand Tenuity. In the era of Grand Culmen, it was bestowed upon the Celestial Emperor of the Grand Tenuity. In the era of Grand Prime, it was bestowed upon the Celestial Emperor of the Golden Watchtower and the Prime Minister, the Lord of the Azure Youth. These were the transmissions of the middle perfected.

For the transmission of teachings in later ages, there are twelve categories of the responsive and transformative Dharma-gate: (1) the original texts of the Three Caverns, (2) numinous talismans and proclamations, (3) jade instructions and secret taboos, (4) spirit diagrams and illustrations, (5) the transmission of the Dao through the ages, (6) precepts and prohibitions to prevent transgressions, (7) dignified deportment and orderly conduct, (8) methods of cultivation, (9) extended numerologies and hidden sceneries, (10) records and transmissions for instruction, (11) hymns of praise and eulogies, and (12) memorials and petitions. When the Three Caverns are thoroughly understood and responses manifest through talismanic verification, this is the transmission of the teaching in later ages.

In the era of Shaohao, Lord Lao descended upon Mount Kongtong, styled the Responsive Master, and expounded the *Scripture of Solemn Respect*, teaching compliance with the seasons. In the era of Zhuanxu, he descended upon Mount Heng, styled the Vermilion Perfected, and expounded the *Scripture of Subtle Words*, teaching the Way of loyalty and compliance. In the era of Emperor Ku, he descended by the riverside, styled the Keeper of Diagrams, and expounded the *Scripture of the Yellow Court*, teaching the Way of purity and harmony. He also commanded the Perfected Kings of the Nine Heavens, the Perfected Sovereigns of the Three Heavens, bearing the staffs of Nine Lights and the talismans of Scenic Clouds, to descend to the Terrace of Virtue and bestow upon Emperor Ku the *Three Heavenly Treasure Talismans of the Nine Heavens’ Numinous Perfected*, to be offered above to Heaven, ensuring the Two Modes were without omission, and below to nurture humanity, ensuring lifespans were without decline.

The Emperor then performed the Heavenly sacrifice upon the altar by the Northern River, concealing the talismans upon the peaks of Mount Zhong. Later, he ascended to Heaven and became the Perfected of the Mysterious Palace. At that time, the Lord Lao transmitted the Dao to Red Pine Master, Clothed-in-Robes Master, Wang Ni, and Nibbling Secrets. This is briefly recorded in the *Tang Annals*.

According to the *Wei Shu: Treatise on Buddhism and Daoism*, the origins of the Daoist school trace back to Lord Lao, who preceded Heaven and Earth to nourish the myriad beings. Above, he dwells in Jade Capital as the ancestral deity of spirit-kings; below, he resides in Purple Tenuity as the sovereign of flying immortals. His transformations are boundless, his virtue both manifest and concealed; responding to stimuli, he adapts without fixed form. He bestowed teachings upon the Xuanyuan Emperor at Mount Emei and instructed Emperor Ku at the Terrace of Virtue. Great Yu inquired of the secrets of longevity, while Yin Xi received the essentials of the *Dao and Virtue*. The cinnabar-scripted, purple-charactered *Scripture of Ascending the Mysterious and Treading the Void*, the jade, stone, and golden-light *Wondrous Existence and Cavernous Numinosity*—such texts are too numerous to recount.

The *Sui Shu: Treatise on Classics and Books* corroborates: Since ancient times, the likes of the Yellow Emperor, Emperor Ku, and Xia Yu all encountered divine beings and received the registers of the Dao. As the ages grew distant, their traces vanished from histories and records. It further states: The teachings beyond the mundane are the profound attainments of sages. When vulgar scholars engage with them, failing to grasp their essence, they often adulterate them with absurdities—this is the source of their corruption. Thus, the teachings of the *Doctrine of the Mean* are rarely expounded, yet they cannot be dismissed as false.

In the era of Emperor Yao, he descended upon Mount Gushe, styled Master Accomplished-in-Service, and expounded the *Scripture of Mysterious Virtue*, teaching the Way of humility and deference. In the era of Emperor Shun, he descended by the River’s banks at Heyang, styled Master Yin Longevity, and expounded the *Scripture of the Dao and Virtue*, teaching the Way of non-action. He also transmitted the Dao to Master Peng. This is recorded in the *Tang Annals*.

Per the *Extensive Records of the Taiping Era*, the *Collected Accounts of Immortals* states: The Daoist adept Wang Miaoxiang dwelled on Mount Jiuyi in Cangwu, practicing grain abstention and qi refinement, ever reciting the *Yellow Court Scripture* and offering dawn devotions with utmost sincerity. Suddenly, a fragrant mist arose, dense and divine, while auspicious clouds filled the courtyard. Heavenly music resounded through the skies, and radiant light illuminated the altar hall. A thousand chariots and ten thousand riders descended from the void, their banners and crane-canopied parasols heralding the brush of nine dragons, alighting before the altar. There appeared a transcendent official, clad in feathered robes and a bejeweled crown, girded with a sword and trailing celestial slippers, ascending the dais to sit. His body emanated five-colored light. Miaoxiang approached to pay homage.

The transcendent addressed her: "I am the sovereign of the ancient Youyu clan, Emperor Shun. Having wearied of governing the myriad states, I cultivated the Dao upon this mountain, ever desiring to guide later generations toward enlightenment. Yet the world holds none worthy of instruction. The Dao resides within, not without; it abides in your own person, not in others. As the *Mysterious Scripture* states: 'Cultivate it within yourself, and your virtue shall be true.'

Recently, the Earthly Bureau reported that you have dwelled upon this mountain for over thirty years, steadfast from beginning to end, guarding the Dao without deviation, preserving sincere devotion and upholding the mysterious precepts. Were you to achieve no realization, this would be the Dao’s abandonment of you. Yet the *Mysterious Scripture* declares: 'Ever excelling in saving beings, it abandons none.' The Dao’s benevolence is universal, desiring the perfection of all things and the salvation of all people. However, worldly beings, their fortune and virtue meager, their Dao-qi shallow, cannot persist in diligent and enduring practice.
