Upon examining the classics, the evidence shines forth clearly: the conversion of the barbarians is factual, and the scripture is not false. *Futu* is the Buddha, and the transformation of customs surely required a scripture. Yet the sages, in establishing teachings, respond to circumstances and act accordingly. Moreover, the natures of middling and superior persons differ, and the gates of Dao and Buddha open in accord with their dispositions. Is it not fitting that the two teachings flow together in vast harmony?”

The Gentleman for Court Audiences, Acting Right Reminder of the Hongwen Academy, Zhang Sidao, presented his argument:

“Lord Lao manifested in the Eastern Lands and disseminated his teachings in the West—events recorded in earlier texts, traces evident in past deliberations. The conversion of the barbarians is factual, and the scripture is not false. Its words encompass what preceded heaven and earth, its principles arise beyond the patterns of literary refinement. At times, it humbly engages with the world, thereby inaugurating the school of yielding and weakness.”

At times, he scrutinizes faults with unyielding clarity, thereby subduing the force of rigidity. Adapting teachings to circumstances, his sublime intent is beyond measure; prescribing remedies for afflictions, his sagely efficacy is unfathomable.

Court Gentleman for Ceremonial Service, Acting Palace Steward of the Heir Apparent and Concurrent Academician of the Hongwen Academy, Zhang Yuanjian, presented his argument:

“The Great Dao is all-pervading, responding to stimuli wherever they arise—be it among the Hu or the Han; it merely turns within this very body. Dwelling in the Central Lands, it spreads the true wind of purity and stillness; journeying to the Western Rong, it manifests wondrous transformations.”

Court Gentleman for Miscellaneous Uses, Acting Gentleman of the Curved Pantry of the Heir Apparent and Grand Pillar of State, Zhang Taiyuan, presented his argument:

“The Dao originated in the Central Lands, while the Buddha’s teachings descended in the Western Regions. Though teachings are established according to place, they share the same essence under different names. Moreover, Lord Lao’s transformations are boundless—now appearing in heaven as an emperor, now in the world as a master—revealing forms in accord with beings, his numinous responses beyond reckoning. Even if historical records lack evidence, the Buddha’s teachings differ not from Lord Lao’s.”

Supervisor of the Imperial University, Academician Wang Fanghui, presented his argument, citing the *Records of the Grand Historian*:

“When Laozi crossed the pass, he expounded the *Classic of the Dao and Virtue* in over five thousand words to Yin Xi, then vanished without trace. Liu Xiang’s *Biographies of the Immortals* states: ‘Laozi cultivated qi, prized namelessness, and in time entered the Great Qin.’ Thus we know him as a true sage.”

Supervisor of the Imperial University, Erudite Wu Yanghao, presented his argument, citing the *Records of the Grand Historian*:

“Laozi was a man of Chu, who served as Archivist during the Shang era. When Confucius journeyed to Zhou to inquire about ritual, Laozi said: ‘The man of whom you speak has long since turned to dust; only his words remain. I have heard that a skilled merchant hides his wealth as if empty, while a gentleman of abundant virtue appears simple. Shed your arrogance and excess desires, for they profit you nothing. This is all I have to tell you.’ Confucius returned and told his disciples: ‘Today I saw Lord Lao—was he not like a dragon?’ When Laozi left the pass, Yin Xi said: ‘You are about to withdraw from the world; I beg you to write a book for me.’ Thereupon he composed the *Classic of the Dao and Virtue* in over five thousand words, then vanished without trace. Some say he lived to one hundred and sixty, others to twelve hundred—none can verify it. Liu Xiang’s *Biographies of the Immortals* also states: ‘Laozi cultivated qi, prized namelessness, and in time entered the Great Qin.’ Thus we know him as a sage.”

Academician of the Hongwen Academy, Granted the Purple Gold Fish Bag, Yuan Banqian, presented his argument:

“According to Fan Ye’s *Biography of Pei Kai* in the *Later Han History*, the *Wei Chronicle’s Western Regions Transmission*, the *Northern History’s Western Regions Transmission*, and over ten other works from the Zhou, Sui, and other dynasties, all state that Laozi entered the Flowing Sands in the West, and all refer to his conversion of the Hu.”

Academician of the Hongwen Academy and Concurrent Reader-in-Waiting to the Various Princes, Cui Yuanwu, presented his argument:

“According to the Buddhist *Sutra of Universal Radiance and Auspicious Responses*, the *Long Āgama Sutra*, the *Record of the Middle Era*, the *Biographies of Eminent Recluses*, and over ten other works from the Jin, Song, Qi, Liang, Zhou, and Sui dynasties, all state that the Buddha was born in the ninth year of King Zhuang of Zhou, the *guisi* year, on the eighth day of the fourth month.”

On the fifteenth day of the sixth month of the first year of the *Wansui Tongtian* era, an imperial edict declared:

“Lord Lao’s conversion of the Hu is recorded in canonical pronouncements; how dare the monastic community presumptuously petition for its erasure? Thus we know that one-sided words cannot serve as evidence. Matters should be settled through balanced deliberation, and this assembly’s judgment is just. Even if historical records lack evidence, how could court officials falsely affirm it? Clearly, the conversion of the Hu is true, not false.”

According to the *Treatise on Bibliography* in the *New Tang History*, the *Bing* section records *A Memorial on the Laozi’s Conversion of the Hu Sutra* in one fascicle, stating:

“In the first year of the *Wansui Tongtian* era, the monk Huicheng submitted a memorial requesting the destruction of the *Laozi’s Conversion of the Hu Sutra*. An edict ordered the Minister of Justice, Liu Ruxuan, and others to deliberate. Ye Fashan was a native of Chuzhou. At the age of seven, he once fell into water, and his family believed him dead.”

Three years later, he returned. His parents asked the reason, and he replied: “A youth in blue led me to drink the cloud-nectar, then guided me to pay homage to the Most High Lord Lao. The Lord Lao received me and kept me there, which is why I was delayed.” By his twentieth year, he stood nine feet tall, his nature pure and unsullied, abstaining from meat. He often dwelled alone in secluded chambers or roamed forests and marshes. Upon returning from the immortal precincts, he had already mastered the arts of summoning and dispatching spirits, and so he divined a dwelling on the Mao-You Mountain. His gate stood near the mountain, a massive boulder blocking the path; the master cast a talisman, and in an instant the stone flew away, astonishing all who witnessed it.

Once, while traveling through Kuocang and Baima Mountain, he encountered three divine beings in a stone chamber, all clad in brocade robes and jeweled crowns. They addressed the master, saying: “We are commanded by the Most High Lord Lao to convey a secret decree to you. You are originally the Left Immortal Minister of the Purple Tenuity of the Great Ultimate, but for negligence in record-keeping, you were banished to the mortal realm. Swiftly establish merit, aid the people, and assist the state. When your merit is complete, you shall resume your former post. The Orthodox Unity, Three, and Five Methods are now bestowed upon you—strive diligently.” With these words, they departed. From then on, he subdued and eradicated malevolent spirits, ever making the salvation of others his purpose.

Emperor Gaozong summoned him to the capital and offered the rank of *Shangqing*, which he declined, instead requesting ordination as a Daoist priest. Empress Wu later summoned him to the divine capital. When Emperor Zhongzong was restored to the throne, Wu Sansi still held state power. The master, having frequently discerned portents and omens, protected Zhongzong, Prince Xiang, and the future Emperor Xuanzong. Resented by Sansi for this, he was exiled to Nanhai. After a year, he entered the Western Mountains of Hongzhou to cultivate his spirit and practice the Dao.

On the ninth day of the third month in the fourth year of the *Jinglong* era (a *xinhai* year), the three divine beings of Kuocang descended once more, conveying the command of the Most High Lord Lao: “You must assist Our Emperor Ruizong and the sagely sovereign of the *Kaiyuan* era. You cannot remain secluded in the mountains, neglecting your appointed duty.” With these words, they departed. At the time, neither emperor had yet ascended the throne, yet their temple names and reign titles were already foretold to him. In the eighth month of that year, an imperial edict indeed summoned him to court.

Later, after the pacification of Empress Wei, Prince Xiang was enthroned. Ruizong and Xuanzong succeeded to the throne in turn, and all matters of fortune or misfortune, movement or stillness, were invariably reported to him in advance. On one occasion, Tubo envoys presented a treasure, its casket inscribed: *“Let the Emperor open it himself; let no other know the secret.”* The court fell silent, save for Fashan, who said: *“This is an ill-omened casket. Bid the Tubo envoy open it himself.”* Xuanzong followed his counsel. When opened, a crossbow bolt sprang forth, killing the envoy—just as Fashan had foretold.

Shortly thereafter, he was appointed *Yinqing Guanglu Daifu*, *Honglu Qing* with concurrent duties, *Yueguo Gong*, and abbot of Jinglong Abbey. The account in the *Taiping Guangji* matches this precisely.

In the sixth month of the fourth year of the *Jinglong* era (a *gengxu* year), after the consort Wei murdered Zhongzong and usurped imperial authority, she further plotted against Ruizong.

At the time when Minghuang was Prince of Linzi, he plotted to quell the internal crisis but remained uncertain of its outcome. The Lord Lao then transformed himself into a white-robed elder, divining fortunes outside the Chunming Gate. The prince sought a divination, and suddenly a single stalk of millet soared forth, standing erect in midair. The elder laughed and said: *“This hexagram bodes well for seizing the throne and becoming emperor; all else is inauspicious. The advantage lies within three days.”* Thereupon, the prince, together with Liu Youqiu and Zhong Shaojing, finalized their plan to assassinate Empress Wei and enthrone Ruizong. He then ordered a search for the divining elder, but his whereabouts were unknown, nor did anyone realize he was the Lord Lao. A temple was erected on the site, named the “Divine Father Shrine,” with an inscription personally composed and calligraphed by the prince. The people of Chang’an continue to worship there to this day. *Record of Marvels in Luozhong*.

On the fifteenth day of the second month of the third year of the *Kaiyuan* era (a *dingmao* day), Minghuang designated the Lord Lao’s birthday as the Festival of the Mysterious Origin. He composed the *“Eulogy to the Mysterious Origin Emperor”*, which reads:

*Behold the supreme virtue,*
*Born to long years.*
*White locks hang like a minister’s cap,*
*Purple qi floats in the heavens.*
*Abiding in silent radiance,*
*Through endless kalpas unbroken.*
*Ancestor of all teachings,*
*Named the Mysterious Origin.*
*Eastward, he instructed Confucius;*
*Westward, he enlightened the Golden Immortals.*
*A hundred kings took him as their model,*
*His lineage transmitted through successive sages.*
*To the west of the Hangu Pass,*
*He left behind the Five Thousand Characters.*
*The Dao that can be spoken is not the eternal Dao,*
*Mysterious, yet ever more mysterious.*

The emperor personally inscribed the eulogy in *hongfen* script on an eight-part red-lacquered tablet, placing it above the canopy of the Lord Lao’s hall. He issued an edict renaming Yangjiao Mountain as Longjiao Mountain, the temple as Qingtang Abbey, and composed an inscription for its stele. Statues of the six sage emperors—Gaozu, Taizong, Gaozong, Zhongzong, Ruizong, and Xuanzong—were sculpted and arrayed in attendance. Upon his return from the eastern feng sacrifice, the emperor paid homage to the Lord Lao at his former residence in Bozhou, personally transcribing the *Daode Jing* onto stone, erecting a great stele, constructing an octagonal tower, and covering it before the Hall of Emptiness and Non-Being.

In the first year (a *xinyou* year), a withered cypress at the Lord Lao’s former residence in Bozhou had stood for ages, and the Daoist priests intended to fell it. As they chopped the wood, each splinter bore five vermilion characters—*qian yuan heng li zhen*—in exquisitely precise strokes. The matter was reported to the throne, and the emperor decreed: *“The auspicious wood manifests numinous signs; wondrous script appears of its own accord. To proclaim great fortune and bless the grand design, it aligns the five virtues with the *Book of Changes* and welcomes ten thousand generations of propitious destiny. Offer sincere thanks and report this to the historiographers.”* The splinters were stored in the imperial treasury and bestowed upon the imperial princes, chief ministers, and Daoist clergy.

In the third month, a stone stele was erected at Jinglong Abbey, and the emperor commanded the Daoist priest Sima Chengzhen of Mount Tiantai to inscribe the Lord Lao’s *Daode Jing* in the three scripts of Cai Yong’s stone classics. Today, a lacquered version remains at Chongdao Abbey on Mount Tiantai, also transcribed by Ziming himself.

In the eleventh year (a *guihai* year), the prefecture of Pu reported that during the construction of the Mysterious Origin Temple, a jade stone shaped like a half-moon was unearthed, its reverse depicting an immortal pounding medicine. When struck, its sound was clear and resonant. The emperor ordered it sent to the Mysterious Origin Abbey in Taiyuan Prefecture, naming it the “Recumbent Moon Chime,” to be struck only during purification and offering rites. Later, Zhang Qi, the military governor of the eastern capital, reported that during the renovation of the Ancient Abbey of Immortal Residence in Lushan County, Ruzhou, a jade chime was discovered, its sound audible for miles. It was ordered placed in the Hall of the Sacred Ancestor at Taiqing Palace for use in the altar of purification rites—now classified among the “cloud plates.”

During the construction of an abbey in Quzhou, a fish three feet long was unearthed while digging. It resembled iron, with a faint purple-green hue, its luster like jade, its carving seemingly beyond human craft. When struck, it resonated deeply. Unable to identify the fish, it was presented to the court. The emperor displayed it to his officials, but none could recognize it. He then named it the “Auspicious Fish Chime” and ordered it placed in Taiwei Abbey, to be struck during purification lectures. Thereafter, abbeys and temples competed to replicate it in wood and stone as a means to assemble the faithful. The use of wooden fish in abbeys and temples began from this time.

In the ninth month of the fourteenth year, an edict proclaimed: *“The Mysterious Origin Emperor, the divine and sagely patriarch, is the ancestral root of our dynasty. In the earliest chaos, he revealed the mandate of heaven. Gaozu responded, and thus a temple was established at the site of his descent, the county renamed Divine Mountain. Recently, the temple courtyard has repeatedly manifested auspicious signs. Reverently bearing the numinous response, we rejoice deeply. Let the prefecture select seven devout Daoist priests to purify themselves, burn incense, and offer reverence at the temple on Longjiao Mountain.”*

On the eighth day of the fourth month of the seventeenth year, a vegetarian feast was held at the newly established Xinxing Convent in Xinjin County, Shuzhou. A Daoist priest arrived late and took his seat. The assembled monks slighted him and did not offer food. The Daoist slowly rose, entered the main hall, and did not emerge for a long time. After the feast concluded, the monks entered the hall to search for him, but no trace remained.

Suddenly, a divine image emerged within the temple pillar, its form concealed yet distinct. When carved with a knife, it became even more refined and exquisite. The eyebrows, whiskers, and hair were as delicate as if painted, wearing a floral coronet and rosy garments. Upon the coronet rested an object resembling a mandarin duck. Beneath the square-toed shoes, lotus flowers appeared, and behind the flowers, a lotus leaf, upon which sat a tortoise. Behind the left elbow, within a cloud-like lotus flame, a dragon’s head manifested. Before the right shoulder, a tiger turned its gaze to the left. Surrounding the entire body was a radiant flame, with cloud leaves and celestial flowers above, and a great flower like a canopy shading the form.

Zhang Jingzhong, Chief Administrator of the Yi Prefecture Grand Protectorate, memorialized: *“Within the jurisdiction of this office, at the Xinxing Convent in Xinjin County, Shuzhou, a natural wood grain in the pillar of the Buddha hall has subtly risen to form the sacred image of the Venerable Lord Lao. Atop the head is a floral canopy, and beneath the feet, before and behind, thirteen instances of cloud leaves and celestial flowers appear.”*

The appointed investigating officer, Wang Dazhong, verified and reported, together with Shuzhou Prefect Li Zhongxun, Vice Prefect Lu Fang, County Magistrate Li Shao, Daoist priests, Buddhist monks, and nuns—one hundred thirty persons in all—that: *“The natural wood grain has indeed revealed a true visage, divinely near and wondrously subtle. The more it was washed and carved, the clearer it became—beyond what painting could achieve, beyond what carving could attain.”*

We humbly submit that the Most High Lord Lao, the Great Sage of Primordial Heaven, is ever-changing and unpredictable, his hidden manifestations unfathomable. It is further said: *“Auspicious flowers encircle it, their fragrance unceasing; the floral canopy floats above, its luminous treasure ever noble. Manifesting upon the temple pillar, it seems to mark the year of the Historian’s Record; illuminating the Buddhist shrine, it faintly recalls the day of the Hu-conversion. Though the phoenix nested in the Xuanyuan Hall, and the qilin crouched in the Zhou court, how could they compare to the descent of the Divine Ancestor and the mandate borne by his sagely descendant?”*

We beseech that this be joyfully recorded in the Nine Ancestral Temples, its glory matched to the Two Principles, inscribed by the historiographers, and proclaimed throughout the realm.

On the twenty-fourth day of the fifth month, the eunuch Lin Zhaoyin was dispatched to Shu to retrieve the image-pillar. A precious palanquin was prepared, and upon its arrival in the capital, it was installed in the Great Harmony Hall for three days of reverent obeisance. After the grand vegetarian feast concluded, the Chamberlain for the Palace Revenues was ordered to transfer it to the Eastern Brightness Abbey for display and veneration, permitting both officials and commoners to pay their respects. It was then decreed that the Daoist abbeys of the Two Streets each host it for seven days before returning it to the palace.

The imperial edict proclaimed: *“The Dao’s essence is boundless; the Primordial Origin responds. Its form appears in the pillar of the Historian, its name timely in Xinxing. The ancestral temples bestow favor; the living beings receive blessing. Let it be recorded in the Historiographer’s Office and announced to the four quarters.”*

In the tenth month of the eighteenth year, the Emperor commanded Chen Xilie, Academician of the Jixian Institute, and others to lecture on the *Daoist Scripture of Virtue and Power* in the Three Palaces. The President of the Chancellery, Pei Guangting, memorialized: *“Yao and Shun governed through deference, while Tang and Wu rose by force of arms. Some wearied their spirits and bodies, others taxed their minds with anxiety. Though the living kind may have glimpsed a measure of peace, the wind of non-action has yet to attain the Great Dao. Now Your Majesty’s transformative governance has harmonized with the mysterious Dao, diminishing the nearness of action while magnifying the teaching of wordless instruction. This is to cast aside ornament and return to the root, to strip away falsity and preserve truth. Such a path lies only in the realm of virtue and power, firmly within the arts of Laozi and Zhuangzi.”*

Thereupon, the Emperor commanded Chen Xilie, Academician of the Jixian Institute and Drafter of the Secretariat; Wang Jiongzhi, Remonstrance Advisor; Kang Ziyuan, Vice Minister of the Court of the Imperial Clan and Lecturer-in-Waiting; and Feng Chaoyin, Grand Master for Exemplary Service, to attend lectures in the Three Palaces, expounding the true scripture and elucidating the Seven Sages of Xiangcheng and the Four Masters of Gushan. In governance, may the wind of purity and stillness prevail; in self-cultivation, may the way of long life and enduring vision be attained. The sagely transformation and mysterious mandate bring joy and peace to the realm, so that all live by it unawares—a rarity unseen in ages past. As one unworthy of my office, I humbly request that this be inscribed in the historical records and proclaimed throughout the land.

The Emperor responded by hand: *“I reverently uphold the ancestral succession and humbly bear the mandate of heaven, ever vigilant day and night, fearful of inadequacy. I seek worthy ministers to entrust with counsel, and extend invitations to learned scholars to consult their vast knowledge, that they may support my shortcomings and harmonize all things. Within, there is peace; without, there is accomplishment. Punishments are just, and lawsuits cease. With leisure in my serene repose, I turn my attention to the classics. I hold that the Dao is the mystery of mysteries, and virtue the foundation of teaching and transformation. By lecturing on its subtle meanings and examining its secret texts, may governance be achieved through non-action, and things respond without coercion. How dare I compare my virtue to Yao and Shun, or measure my achievements against Yu and Tang? Yet I must first rectify my heart, deeply reflecting on what is distant and near, striving to unify customs and extend this to the myriad people. Only if all return to purity and stillness, and together uphold the profound silence, will the compilation and proclamation you propose be truly timely.”*

On the night of the fifteenth day of the second lunar month in the nineteenth year, the Emperor dreamed of a divine being who addressed him, saying: “I am the Messenger of the Nine Heavens, sent by the Jade Emperor of the Primordial True One—who is none other than your ancestor, the Most High Lord Lao. He has commanded me to oversee the Three Realms, Ten Directions, Nine Heavens, and Nine Earths as the Inspector-General of the Turning Wheel. The Director of Destinies of the Nine Heavens resides in the hidden mountains of Shu; the Venerable Elder of the Nine Heavens dwells in the Azure City of Shu; and I abide on Mount Lu by the Jiang. Temples may be erected in these three places. Five hundred years hence, blessings shall extend to all living beings.”

At dawn, the Emperor rose, burned incense, and bowed in gratitude toward the empty sky. Suddenly, the divine figure reappeared amidst the clouds, attended by an ethereal retinue. He commanded Wu Daozi to depict the vision as seen, and dispatched envoys bearing tribute to the three mountains to establish shrines.

On the first day of the spring month in the twenty-first year, the cyclical day *gengzi*, an edict was issued: “Laozi’s *Dao De Jing* should be kept in every household of scholars and commoners. Each year, candidates for the imperial examinations shall be tested on one or two passages from the *Book of Documents* or the *Analects*, with an equal number of questions on the *Dao De Jing*, so as to honor the root of the Dao and broaden the wellspring of transformation. This present decree should likewise be kept in every home, to be reflected upon thrice daily, that my intent may be known.”

The Vice-Director of the Chancellery, Pei Guangting, and others memorialized: “We have witnessed Your Majesty’s recent edict, instructing the hundred officials and extending to the myriad people. Your sagely grace is vast and boundless, your virtue and beneficence like heaven itself. Having nurtured all life, you now exhort and encourage, so that none fail to turn toward goodness, all knowing the proper direction. Though unworthy, we serve at the pivot of governance, yet have done little to advance the common good. Suddenly, we receive this celestial favor, as if scales had fallen from our eyes. Even the august sovereigns of high antiquity—Fu Xi, Shen Nong, Yao, and Shun—could not surpass this. The realm is most fortunate. We humbly request that this be recorded in the national history, to be shown to future generations.”

The Emperor assented, replying by edict: “The teachings of the Primordial True One are the foundation of family and state. Not merely to honor my ancestors, but to uphold the root of the Dao, I have chosen the first day of the new year, the beginning of spring, to issue this decree on governance through purity and stillness, trusting that the chief ministers will carry it out. In selecting officials, one should first seek those of simple and unadorned virtue.”

In the twelfth month, the Lecturer-in-Waiting Chen Xilie and others concluded their recitation of the classics. The Vice-Director of the Chancellery and concurrent Director of the Chancellery and Department of State Affairs, Pei Yaoqing, and others memorialized: “We have witnessed Your Majesty’s completion of the *Book of Documents*, the *Book of Changes*, the *Dao De Jing*, and the works of Zhuangzi and Liezi. Your sagely heart embraces the Dao; your imperial instruction exalts the Confucian tradition. The profound influence of the Dao now reaches far, beginning anew from this moment. Moreover, your concerns extend to the four seas, your thoughts to the ten thousand regions. Each day after the morning audience, you retire to the inner palace to study the classics; with the wind at your back, you open the way for the people, even lecturing in the traveling palace. Not even the Han emperors in a single night could surpass this. Having grasped the essence of Laozi and Zhuangzi, you act with benevolence and forbearance, aligning all things. With the heart of Yao and Shun, you examine antiquity and establish models for governance. Though you delve deeply, your progress is swift without haste. You harmonize the myriad beings, bringing joy to all things. Your great plans illuminate the records of history, their brilliance enduring. Though unworthy, we have been privileged to offer counsel and receive your august words. Our joy and reverence are beyond measure. We humbly request that this be proclaimed by the court historians, that your glorious deeds may be celebrated.”

The Emperor replied by hand: “The *Book of Documents* is refined and solemn; the *Book of Changes* is subtle and profound. From childhood, I studied under teachers but have not yet plumbed their deepest meanings, hence my frequent lectures. As for the *Dao De Jing*, its layers unfold endlessly. Examining its intent, one finds countless connections. Having inquired into the Way of Guangchengzi, I have also gained the guidance of Fangming. In this age, such an opportunity comes but once in a thousand years. Thus, I have expounded these principles to enlighten you.”

The civil and military officials, led by the Right Chancellor and Academician of the Jixian Institute, Xiao Song, and others memorialized: “Since last year, by Your Majesty’s edict, the Academicians of the Jixian Institute—Vice Minister of Works Chen Xilie, Remonstrance Official Wang Jiongzhi, and Director of the Bureau of Sacrifices Feng Chaoyin—have daily attended lectures on the *Dao De Jing* of the Primordial August Emperor, as well as the *Book of Changes*, the *Book of Documents*, and the *Zhuangzi*, concluding on the twenty-fourth day of this month. We have heard that Yao gathered the texts of former ages to perfect his sagacity, and Shun observed the images of antiquity to manifest his wisdom. Thus, we know that the Dao is worthy of reverence, and ritual forgets its own nobility. Not merely to assemble learning, but to guide the people. Your Majesty’s wisdom is truly divine, your actions truly sagely. The influence of the Dao is perfectly harmonious; cultural instruction is fully realized. Yet you still seek to broaden your knowledge and accumulate learning, examining antiquity in all matters, delving into the subtleties of the classics. You honor your ancestors by studying the scriptures of Laozi, embodying heaven by observing the images of the *Book of Changes*. You pursue the teachings of Guangchengzi through the chapters of Zhuangzi, and investigate the old rites of the Tang through the *Canon of Yao*. Recently, you offered sacrifices to the Earth Goddess in the north and traveled to the hot springs in the east. Though the land was crossed by wind and sand, or the sky threatened with cold and snow, the lecture hall was always convened, the traveling palace unchanged. This suffices to show your love of learning and your diligent virtue. Even Fu Xi’s drawing of the trigrams or Yu’s reception of the scriptures cannot compare. Though unworthy, we stand in the court and have heard the imperial Way. We humbly request that this be recorded by the court historians and proclaimed throughout the realm.”

The Emperor replied by hand: “I have heard that the Academicians of the Jixian Institute, after the morning audience, regularly engage in lectures on the Confucian and Daoist classics—this is their usual duty. Over the months and years, I have studied their chapters and verses. The refined admonitions of the *Book of Documents* are examined in light of antiquity and tested against the present. The *Dao De Jing* is drawn from the true and does not exalt its own teachings. Is this not the essence of governing the state? Let it be recorded by the court historians, as you have requested.”

On the *guiwei* day of the third month in the twenty-third year, the Emperor personally annotated the *Laozi* and composed an exegesis in eight fascicles, along with the *Kaiyuan Textual Phonology* in thirty fascicles. These were distributed to the public officials, scholars, commoners, and the Daoist and Buddhist communities, with instructions to offer candid opinions on their merits.

The civil and military officials, led by the Right Chancellor Xiao Song, memorialized: “In accordance with Your Majesty’s edict, we have consulted all offices and disseminated the texts to Daoists and Buddhists. The reports we have received all affirm that the profound words delve into subtleties, and the compilation of characters is comprehensive and harmonious. Once published, they will serve as a model for future generations, revering your sagely regulations. Observing the mysterious and knowing the constant, they embody the essence of the sacred altar. Long-standing doubts and past errors are corrected in every detail, fully illuminating the teachings of the Dao and extending the influence of Confucianism. Having already transformed the people, they also establish the foundation. We are deeply fortunate.”

Though diverse interpretations were sought and the celestial will awaited, the realm shares a single script and a unified discourse—no alternative phrasing need be considered. We humbly request that these be compiled into the historical records and preserved in the imperial archives.” The Emperor granted his approval.

In the twelfth month of the twenty-seventh year, the chief ministers Niu Xianke and Li Linfu memorialized: “We have reverently observed the Crown Prince conveying Your Majesty’s virtuous decree to the Historiographer’s Office. We have learned that on the fifth day of the previous month, as Your Majesty prepared to tour the northern banks of the Wei River, that very night you dreamed of the August First Emperor of the Mysterious Origin, who said: ‘Tomorrow, my child, do you intend to journey north? The spirits are not present there—this matter should be halted. At the fifth watch, there shall be a sign.’ And he added: ‘You have already reigned for many years—why must it be this day?’ Your Majesty then issued an edict at the second watch to cancel the northern tour of the Wei. At the fifth watch, a fierce gale indeed arose, subsiding only at dusk.

We reflect that no virtue surpasses the imperial standard in embodying the numinous truth, and no governance excels that of our August Emperor. Thus, through profound resonance, the sagely and the divine converge. Unfathomable words foretold an inevitable outcome: the violent winds confirmed the prophetic dream. This not only manifests the longevity of Your Majesty’s reign but also heralds boundless blessings—enduring as heaven and earth, as certain as a tally’s verification. From the dawn of civilization, we have scoured the annals and examined the omens: never has there been a sign so luminously evident as this.

We, unworthy as we are to serve near the throne and to hold the office of historiographer, have been privileged to witness this virtuous decree. Our joy knows no bounds.”

In the fourth month of the twenty-eighth year, the Emperor dreamed that Lord Lao said: “I have an image located over a hundred *li* southwest of the capital. Send someone to seek it, for I shall meet you at the Palace of Flourishing Celebration, where great fortune awaits you.” The following day, he addressed his chief ministers: “For nearly thirty years since ascending the throne, I have never failed to rise at cock’s crow to pay reverent homage to the true visage and pray for the people’s blessings. Recently, while offering such homage before dawn had broken, I sat in quiet meditation and dozed. There, the August First Emperor appeared and dispatched an emissary, along with the Daoist master of ceremonies Xiao Yuanyu, to search. They arrived at the Louguan Temple on Mount Zhongnan in Aowuwu County, where they beheld purple clouds descending and a white radiance connecting earth to heaven. Digging beneath, they indeed discovered a jade image of Lord Lao, over three *chi* in height, which they presented to me.

That very day, I happened to be at the Palace of Flourishing Celebration, where I personally received and enshrined the image in the inner hall. It was exactly as I had seen in my dream. I then commanded the chief ministers to view it, who subsequently submitted a memorial of congratulation: ‘The Great Sage of the Mysterious Origin has manifested his true visage—a sign of resonance that truly accords with Your Majesty’s sagely virtue. You embody the Way of utmost truth and honor the source of purity and stillness. How could you not offer reverent prayers for the people’s blessings? Thus, the true visage appeared in your dream, and the august ancestor displayed his numinous power. The search to the southwest confirmed the dream’s promise.

Moreover, the Palace of Flourishing Celebration was once the former residence of the Dragon’s Portent, where the imperial enterprise was founded. That the meeting was foretold in this place, coinciding with its auspicious name, signifies that this image descends from the Purple Palace to guard our imperial house, inaugurating boundless blessings and fulfilling the promise of great fortune. Your Majesty has now consecrated the main hall as a dharma sanctuary—an act of utmost reverence and veneration. Such extraordinary rites shall bring myriad blessings, extending beyond all bounds to encompass the multitudes in shared celebration.

What fortune is ours to have personally witnessed and paid homage! The image’s sublime features defy description. Since the dawn of time, no such event has been recorded in the annals. We humbly request that this be proclaimed throughout the realm and inscribed in the imperial records.’”

The Emperor responded by hand with an edict, saying: “That which is true in dreams is called communion with the divine. Now the sacred countenance has indeed responded to sincerity—how could this be due to my virtue, when it is the great Dao that thus flourishes? Reflecting again on the numinous presence, its words still ring in my ears, promising blessings and merits that shall multiply with each generation. At first, it was announced that the divine would appear in the temporary palace, yet it manifested directly within the inner hall, coinciding with this great celebration, which rightly belongs to my person alone. Consulting the Daoist scriptures, I find this to be a treasure. It is fitting that I nurture the myriad people and repay the divine luminosity.

You, my esteemed ministers, should share my intent: let us proclaim this auspicious response, for how could I dare to decline? On the day *gengxu* of the fifth month, I commanded the relevant officials to depict the true countenance and distribute it throughout the realm. Thereupon, I issued this edict:

The great Dao, formless and complete, precedes heaven and earth. The sages established its teachings to illuminate the ultimate origin, thereby unfolding its wondrous essence and broadly aiding living beings, awakening those of steadfast intent and guiding the lost back to the Way. In thus saving all things, none are abandoned. Who, then, is most worthy of this? None but our illustrious ancestor, the August Prime Emperor of the Mysterious Origin.

I have inherited this sacred enterprise and further expounded the profound Dao. Since ascending the throne, I have, without fail, day and night, purified my thoughts and concentrated my mind, fasting in body and spirit to pay homage before the true countenance. Before dawn, I complete these rites, and this has continued for nearly thirty years—all for the sake of the common people, to pray for abundant blessings. Yet I never imagined that my humble sincerity would reach above, and the sagely visage would deign to observe me. Recently, in a moment of rest, I suddenly dreamed of the true countenance. Upon waking, its radiant form remained before me, its sublime features natural and in perfect accord with the dream. Truly, it has secretly descended from the immortal realm to eternally guard the mortal world, announcing to me boundless blessings. Its virtuous voice still resounds in my ears, revealing to me this extraordinary fortune.

Since the numinous has set its appointed time, and the vast heavens have mysteriously aided it, the ancestral altars and the state shall store up blessings—how could my meager virtue have brought about such an event? To leave it unaddressed would be to neglect reverence. Therefore, I command the relevant officials to immediately copy the true countenance and send it to the Investigating Commissioners of all circuits, who shall then deliver it to the Kaiyuan Temples in each prefecture for installation. The Daoist priests in each locale shall prepare with full ritual decorum to receive it. For seven days and nights after the image’s arrival, they shall hold vegetarian feasts and perform the Daoist rites, and I shall grant funds to each temple to cover the expenses.

From this day forward, let the study and recitation of Daoist scriptures be regularly practiced to elucidate their subtle meanings. The establishment of Daoist academies must be redoubled, with increased encouragement to ensure their flourishing. For the profound truth is vast and far-reaching, and its propagation depends on people. Without such promotion, how can customs be uplifted?

Among all classes of people, those well-versed in the *Daode Jing*, *Zhuangzi*, *Liezi*, *Wenzi*, and the like shall be sought out by local officials and reported by name. I shall personally examine them and bestow special rewards.

Now, the true countenance has manifested—an event unheard of in ancient times. Though its blessings first belong to the state and the imperial house, its joy should be shared equally among officials and commoners. To the imperial princes, princesses, commandery and county ladies, and all civil and military officials within and beyond the court, I shall grant money according to rank. On days of rest and leisure, let them partake in simple meals to express their celebratory joy. The military commissioners and their officers in all circuits shall be treated likewise. The elders of the two capitals and all prefectures shall also receive money to share in this festive banquet, the funds drawn from local government stores.

You, my ministers, from the highest to the humblest, should strive to honor the transformation of the Dao and together restore the wellspring of purity. Let this be proclaimed far and wide, that all may understand my intent.

I have heard it said in the *Doctrine of the Mean*: ‘Sincerity takes form, and form becomes manifest.’ Dreams, too, are the manifestation of sincerity. When King Gaozong of Shang, reverent and silent, pondered the Dao, he dreamed of the Lord on High granting him a worthy assistant—and indeed, he found one. Tradition holds that the August Ming Emperor, in his frequent reverence before the true countenance, was moved to dream of it—such is the manifestation and revelation of sincerity. Yet when he grew weary of governance and entrusted power to unworthy men, it led to the calamity of the Hu barbarians. Some compare him to the First Emperor of Qin and Emperor Wu of Han, claiming their downfalls stemmed from their devotion to the Dao. This I find deeply perplexing.

The Dao is rooted in a pure heart and few desires, and its function lies in aiding others and benefiting all things. Yet these three rulers indulged their inner desires and recklessly waged war, merely seeking through prayers and sacrifices to attain immortality—how could they have succeeded? Consider Emperor Wu of Liang, who exhausted the state’s resources to build pagodas and temples, offered his own body and life as a servant to monks, renounced all joy in the six palaces, and abolished sacrifices in the seven ancestral temples. He personally lectured on the Buddha Maitreya and the living Buddha, with the sage monk Baozhi as his protector—yet he still could not escape the disaster at Taicheng. Could this, too, be blamed on his devotion to the Dao?

On the day *dingchou* of the first month of the twenty-ninth year *xinsi*, I issued this edict: In the time of the Three Sovereigns, the people were simple and honest, for their rulers transformed them through the Dao. Thereafter, governance diverged. Our illustrious ancestor, the August Prime Emperor of the Mysterious Origin, possessed the virtue of a great sage and embodied the essence of the supreme Dao. He composed the Five Thousand Characters to correct the ills of the age, offering a means to govern the state that transcends the *Book of Changes* and the *Appended Judgments*, surpassing even the most eloquent words. I have decreed that every household study this text, that people may turn toward the right path and governance may be achieved without coercion.

Yet I fear that lesser scholars may not grasp its subtle words, so I have further elucidated it to help them awaken, recover from their weaknesses, and perpetuate boundless goodness. In the two capitals and all circuits, let one temple to the August Prime Emperor be established, where annual Daoist fasts and offerings shall be conducted according to ritual. Additionally, let Academies of the August Mystery be founded, with students drawn proportionally from the existing prefectural schools. They shall study the *Daode Jing*, *Zhuangzi*, *Wenzi*, and *Liezi*. Upon completing their studies, they shall be sent to the capital each year for examination, following the precedent for the *mingjing* degree.

Each academy shall appoint one teaching assistant, selected by the local prefect from among all classes of people after careful consideration, and they shall receive modest additional rewards.

In this month, the prefecture of Bozhou reported that in the temple of the August Prime Emperor, nine wells emitted qi that formed clouds, their five colors shimmering in harmony.”

On the *xinmao* day of the second month, the Emperor composed the *Rainbow Skirts and Feathered Plumes Melody* and the *Purple Tenuity Eight Trigrams Dance* to offer at the Great Clarity Palace, esteeming them above the Nine Temples. He also visited the Kaiyuan Abbey in Huaizhou and the Fengxian Abbey in Quexiang at the request of the princes, nobles, and common people, personally paying homage to the two scriptures of the *Daode Jing*. He had great stone steles erected facing each other, following the model of the Great Clarity Palace.

In the ninth month, from the Xingqing Gate tower, the Emperor personally examined candidates for the *Daode Jing*, *Zhuangzi*, *Wenzi*, and *Liezi* degrees. The imperial examination stated: “In my leisure from governance, I often read the *Daode Jing*, *Wenzi*, *Liezi*, and *Zhuangzi*. Their texts are concise yet profound in meaning, their words lofty yet far-reaching in intent. They can order the state and preserve the self. I revere and uphold their teachings to guide the people. You, scholars, who devote yourselves to these texts—I greatly commend you.

Yet the needs of past and present differ, and literary and substantive styles alternate. If one were to govern with non-interference and not act upon external things, implementing the transformations of high antiquity would not suit the way of ruling today. The defense of the times lies in adapting to what is fitting.

Moreover, rites, music, punishments, and governance are the warp of the state, while sagacity, wisdom, benevolence, and righteousness order human relations. If these were abandoned, their purpose would remain unknown. The *Daode Jing* says, ‘Cut off learning and there will be no sorrow,’ which contradicts the teachings of advancing virtue and cultivating conduct. The *Liezi*’s *Power and Fate* says, ‘What merit have you in things?’—this violates the texts of punishing evil and encouraging good. Which of these two principles is incorrect? Which is superior, and which inferior? The *Wenzi* says, ‘Gold accumulates and edges wear away; jade is layered and never exhausted,’ fully expounding its meaning. The *Zhuangzi* says, ‘Tranquility and knowledge mutually nourish each other,’ clearly verifying its words. If one principle could unify all, and both teachings could be jointly upheld, they would become unchanging norms, entrusted to the contemplation of the empty and expectant mind.”

Candidates such as Yao Ziyan, Zhan Neng, and Yuan Zai passed the examination and were each appointed to office.

In the twelfth month, the Emperor issued an edict: “I constantly think of the common people, never forgetting them even in sleep, hoping their households may be sufficient and prosperous, rich and long-lived. The great method of aiding and saving them lies in none other than the Daoist teachings. The Celestial Sage left models, and his subtle words shine resplendently. Following and practicing them, how distant could their response be? Moreover, as the year approaches its end and all things begin to stir, aligning with the harmony of yang, some may yet be preserved through kindness and nurture. It is fitting to command all abbeys throughout the realm, from the first day of the new year until its close, to continuously recite the *Scripture of the Fundamental Boundary*—a text revealed by Lord Lao to enrich the state and pacify the people.

The granddaughter of the Celestial Master of Han, Yulan, dreamed of a red light descending from heaven into her mouth and awoke pregnant. People doubted her, so she split open her abdomen to prove her innocence. An object like a lotus flower emerged from her belly, within which was a golden seal and a plain silk scroll—this was the scripture.

On the *jiayin* day of the first month of the Tianbao era, purple clouds suddenly descended outside the Vermilion Phoenix Gate. Lord Lao, riding a white horse, with two pairs of attendant immortal youths, stood upon the clouds. He addressed the Court Gentleman of the Prince’s Household, Tian Tongxiu, saying: ‘When I departed with Yin Xi for the Flowing Sands, I concealed a golden casket with a numinous talisman in the former residence of Yin Xi at the old pass of Peach Grove. You may report this to the Emperor so he may retrieve it and use it to guard the state.’

Tongxiu relayed this, and the Emperor dispatched the palace attendant Li Zhizhong to supervise Tongxiu in seeking it at the former site of Hangu Pass, south of Taolin County in Shanzhou. Suddenly, a purple cloud and a white hare appeared beneath a withered mulberry tree west of Yin Xi’s old residence. They dug by hand, reaching the water’s edge, where they found a stone casket and a golden coffer inscribed with fine red seal script on jade tablets. The Emperor ordered the Ten Divisions of Music to welcome the sacred talisman through the northern gate into the imperial carriage. From within, five-colored light radiated, illuminating heaven and earth.”

The Emperor ascended the Vermilion Phoenix Tower, clad in mourning robes and imperial crown, holding golden incense burners, and bowed to welcome and enshrine it in the Hall of Numinous Radiance. That night, divine lamps appeared upon the towers, pavilions, and trees, as well as in the empty void above.

At this time, all civil and military officials, along with the imperial clansmen, Daoist and Buddhist followers, and household disciples, submitted memorials, stating that the auspicious talisman’s resonance had manifested, the sacred treasure of the revolving coffer had been revealed, its hidden response aligning with the reign title, preceding heaven without contradiction. They wished to exalt the Emperor’s honorific title to illuminate the canonical rites. The Emperor firmly declined. After repeated memorials were submitted, on the *renshen* day, he issued an edict:

“The descent of the divine blessing must be reciprocated with rites, and in perpetuating the ancestral sacrifices, one must attend in person. Since assuming the throne, I have broadly propagated the Daoist teachings, venerating the transformation of purity and admonition, and spreading the wind of the Mysterious Origin, hoping that its blessings might extend to the common people and the realm attain longevity. Through the years, I have never slackened in diligence. How could my humble sincerity have moved the response, causing the August Ancestor to descend and manifest the numinous mandate, bestowing the sacred talisman? Having sought it in accordance with the words, it was obtained as foretold. Upon its arrival, extraordinary signs indeed appeared. Truly, the mysteries of the Way are ineffable. Yet such a great blessing for the state—how could anything surpass it? This reveals that what the immortals seal, the workings of creation likewise secure. From the beginning, it awaited the revolving coffer for many years, and now the response to the change of reign title aligns as if by tally. The favor of this propitious fortune inspires profound reverence.

Yet the officials, imperial clansmen, and the heir apparent with his brothers have repeatedly petitioned from without, while the black-robed and yellow-robed elders, along with the venerable, have ceaselessly entreated within, wishing to adopt the name *Tianbao* (‘Heavenly Treasure’) in place of *Kaiyuan* (‘Inaugural Origin’). Considering my own inadequacy, how could I be worthy? However, the profound instructions of the Way demand reverent compliance, and the will of the people cannot be refused. To follow heaven and yield to the multitude accords with the principle of supreme impartiality. Respectfully accepting their request, I am deeply humbled. This is all due to the boundless generosity of the Supreme Mystery, the efficacious protection of the hundred spirits, and the harmonious assistance of the August Ancestor, who in hidden accord has renewed the mandate and clearly manifested the omen of eternal prosperity. It is fitting to observe the sacrificial canons and duly offer thanksgiving.”

Thus, on the fifteenth day of the coming month, it was decreed to enshrine the talisman in the Temple of the Mysterious Origin Emperor. Thereupon, the Temple of the Sacred Emperor of the Mysterious Origin was established in the Great Tranquility Ward, its eastern capital located at the former residence in Accumulated Virtue Lane.

On the *xinmao* day of the second month, the Mysterious Origin Emperor was venerated at the new temple, and the capital observed a prohibition on slaughter. On the *bingshen* day, Zhuangzi was posthumously honored as the Perfected Person of Southern Florescence. On the *gengzi* day, the Emperor said: “Since Zhuangzi is now titled the Perfected Person of Southern Florescence, let the works of Wenzi, Liezi, and Gengsangzi be further deliberated by the Secretariat-Chancellery for report.”

The chief ministers memorialized: “Since Zhuangzi is honored as the Perfected Person of Southern Florescence, let Wenzi be titled the Perfected Person of Penetrating Mystery, Liezi the Perfected Person of Empty Vacuity, and Gengsangzi the Perfected Person of Cavernous Spirit. May their works likewise be designated as *True Scriptures*.” This was approved.

On the twentieth day of the month, an edict was issued: “The August Heaven has favored our mandate, and the August Ancestor has descended in spirit. The rites of auspicious manifestation must be preserved in the sacrificial canons. Zhuangzi, Wenzi, Liezi, and Gengsangzi are ranked among the perfected immortals, embodying the empty clarity of the Way. They propagated the sacred teachings of the Mysterious Origin, broadly disseminating the great Dao among humankind. Their subtle words delve into the profoundest meanings, surpassing all other masters in unparalleled excellence. Henceforth, Zhuangzi shall be titled the Perfected Person of Southern Florescence, Wenzi the Perfected Person of Penetrating Mystery, Liezi the Perfected Person of Empty Vacuity, and Gengsangzi the Perfected Person of Cavernous Spirit. Their writings shall be retitled *True Scriptures*. The Academy of Mysterious Learning shall appoint one Erudite and one Instructor, with one hundred students.”

The Vice Director of the Chancellery, Chen Xilie, memorialized: “I have observed that in the gracious edict of the twentieth day of this month, Zhuangzi was titled the Perfected Person of Southern Florescence, and his work retitled *The True Scripture of Southern Florescence*. Its teachings all concern the essentials of nurturing life, elucidating profound mysteries with a hundred thousand words of mystery, tracing the origins of the Daoist scriptures and encompassing the five thousand subtle principles. Formerly, when I had the honor of attending the imperial lectures and expounding the true text on bended knee, upon reaching the seven chapters, Your Majesty remarked: ‘Among them is *The Mainstay of Nurturing Life*—I have already grasped the art of longevity. Next is *The Token of Full Virtue*—how could there be no extraordinary response?’ I kowtowed and replied: ‘Your Majesty’s virtue is full within, and your actions respond without. After your words were spoken, great blessings must follow, as in the later chapter titled *Responding to Emperors and Kings*.’ Now the Mysterious Origin Emperor has indeed manifested the sacred talisman, revealing the boundless fortune of the imperial lineage and embodying the Dao’s foreknowledge of future events. To honor him with titles and display his image is a ritual unheard of in ages past. I have long cherished this scripture, studying and reciting it for over thirty years, performing rites and burning incense to aid the sagely transformation. Having encountered this extraordinary blessing, my joy surpasses all ordinary sentiment. I humbly request that this be recorded by the historiographers to make manifest the numinous response.”

This was permitted.

In the third month, an imperial edict commanded the *Records of the Historian* to include the "Tables of Ancient and Modern Personages," wherein the Mysterious Origin Emperor was elevated to the rank of Supreme Sage. An edict further established one magistrate each for Zhenyuan County in Bozhou, the Temple of the Primordial Heavenly Empress, and the Temple of the Mysterious Origin Emperor.

On the *wuyin* day of the fourth month, an edict proclaimed: “That from which transformation arises is called the Dao; that by which the Dao operates is called virtue. Its meaning is most vast—who but a sage could elucidate it? In the final years of the Zhou, when the age and the Dao alike declined, our illustrious ancestor, the Mysterious Origin Emperor, revealed the wondrous root, drawing forth and guiding living beings. He thereupon composed the five thousand words of the *Mysterious Classic*, to remedy the ills of the age. Its significance surpasses the *Book of Images* and the *Striking the Drum*; its principles penetrate the subtlest mysteries. It is unmatched by any work of myriad generations, nor can the *Six Classics* compare. Yet those who inherit and practice the former tradition, deeming its scrolls few in number, have relegated it to the category of minor scriptures. Its profound words and abstruse purport are thus misnamed and misconstrued.

Henceforth, throughout the realm, apart from students of the *Exalted Mystery* who are to be examined as before, all other candidates tested on the *Classic of the Dao and Virtue* shall cease. The authorities shall select another minor scripture in its stead. Let the *Classic of the Dao* be designated the Upper Scripture, and the *Classic of Virtue* the Lower Scripture, that the Dao may be honored and virtue esteemed, upheld and revered. Let all, near and far, know Our intent.”

Here ends Scroll Eight of the *Sacred Records of the Primordial Origin*.

**Scroll Nine of the *Sacred Records of the Primordial Origin***
*Compiled by the Song Dynasty Master of Observing the Return, the Eminent Scholar Xie Shoubin*

In the ninth month, the Purple Ultimate Palace was established in Qiao Commandery. Following the precedent of the Western Capital, it was designated the Grand Clarity Palace. The temples of the Primordial Celestial August Emperor and the Primordial Celestial August Empress were likewise converted into palaces.

The system of the Grand Clarity Palace: three gates opened to the south in two rows, and three gates opened to the east and west in one row. Halberds were installed at each gate. The main hall had eight bays front and back, with steps at the *mao*, *wu*, and *you* positions, and a place for the distribution of meals. Dragon and sand terraces were laid out, along with chambers for the emperor’s fasting officials, the ducal ministers, the officiating officials, the imperial kitchens, the fasting kitchens, and the residences of the palace staff.

On the *wuxu* day of the twelfth month, the emperor visited the Huaqing Palace. Suddenly, the Lord Lao appeared above the Audience of the Primordial Pavilion, vanishing after the passage of a moment. Thereupon, the Audience of the Primordial Pavilion was renamed the Pavilion of the Descended Sage.

The emperor saw that the divine talisman bore the inscription “Celestial Treasure, Ten Thousand Years.” The characters “Celestial Treasure” had already presaged the change of the reign title. Thus, he issued an edict to alter the term “year” to “cycle” to accord with it. He also renamed Taolin County as Lingbao County, established the Celestial Treasure Abbey, and had the imperial composition *Inscription on the Divine Talisman* erected there.

In the fourth month of the fourth cycle, on the *guisi* day, an edict proclaimed: “To honor ancestors and serve the departed, reverence is essential; to distinguish rites and rectify ceremonies, propriety must follow the dictates of sentiment. We reflect that the Great Sage Ancestor, the August Emperor of the Primordial Mystery, ascended to heaven in a cloud of *qi*, attaining long life and enduring vision. His sacred form, profound and unfathomable, merges with the boundless transformations of the Mystery. His true countenance has repeatedly manifested, and celestial treasures have gathered in succession. In reverent awe of his blessings, which truly endure forever, We observe that in the rituals at the Grand Clarity Palace, all participants don the full ceremonial regalia. Yet when it comes to the presentation of music, the old names remain unchanged. Moreover, at the time of offerings, the invocation of the *jia* spirit is still recited—this is neither the proper rite for the living nor the fitting ceremony for the descent of immortals. Since the true countenance is peerless and the rites for the unseen differ from those for the manifest, there are reasons of principle that call for adaptation. Henceforth, in all rituals conducted at the Grand Clarity Palace and its affiliated palaces, officials shall don court robes instead, and the invocation tablets shall be discontinued. The words of the offerings and the music to be performed shall be composed by Us personally. The relevant authorities shall prepare the ritual protocols and submit them for Our review.”

The emperor composed the melodies *Descending Perfection* and *Summoning the Immortal*, as well as *Purple Tenuity* and *Escorting the Immortal*, to be performed at the Grand Clarity Palace. By edict, the “Three Bows” were changed to “Three Reverences,” and the invocation tablets were replaced with “blue petitions,” written in vermilion on azure paper. The emperor’s signature was to read, “The Hereditary Emperor, Your Subject So-and-So,” to be observed as the permanent standard.

In the intercalary sixth month of the seventh cycle, on the *bingyin* day, the emperor personally paid homage at the Grand Clarity Palace, bestowing upon the August Ancestor, the August Emperor of the Primordial Dao, the exalted title *August Ancestor, Great Dao, August Emperor of the Primordial Mystery*.

On the *bingchen* day, an edict declared: “The wondrous original texts of the Mysterious Ancestor contain subtle words indeed, transmitting models for learning and propagating the supreme transformation. For this reason, We dispatched envoys to seek the Dao, sending them far and wide to search and collect. In moments of respite from governance, We personally examined the texts. Having corrected errors and emended the volumes, We now ensure their elucidation to honor and encourage the Dao. Let all Daoist scriptures now issued from the palace be copied by the Academy of the Exalted Mystery and distributed to the Commissioners for the Collection of Scriptures in the various circuits, who shall in turn have them transcribed within their jurisdictions. The official copies shall remain with the commissioners, who shall personally encourage recitation in the prefectures.

No teaching of the sages precedes that of the Dao, and every school must have its master. Confucius and the Sage Ancestor flourished at the same time, both serving as the foremost teachers of their traditions. Though comparing their words and virtues defies easy description, the traces of Confucius inquiring about rites and receiving instruction are well attested. Reflecting on the meaning of ‘repeatedly’ and honoring the unity of the exalted, We decree that in the Palace of the Grand Tenuity, before the image of the Sage Ancestor, an additional likeness of Confucius shall be installed, standing with the Four Perfected Ones to his left and right.”

On that day, a general amnesty was declared. The edict read: “The rites of seasonal sacrifices maintain proper order, while changes in substance and form adapt to the times. Our dynasty traces its lineage to the immortal clan and inherits its legacy from the Sage Ancestor. With accumulating prosperity and repeated blessings, We have bestowed boundless favor. It is fitting to establish an enduring ritual for the shared veneration of the divine. Henceforth, at every seasonal sacrifice, the proper arrangement of positions shall be set before the Sage Ancestor in the Grand Clarity Palace. Above, this will clarify the rites of terrestrial pairing to reverently follow the Mysterious Ancestor; below, it will fully express the sincerity of devotion without transgressing the supreme Dao. In the past, seasonal sacrifices were sometimes suspended during the regular offerings, a practice that, while convenient, may have compromised the completeness of ritual. Hereafter, at every seasonal sacrifice, the regular offerings shall consist of plain food, and the triple presentation of incense shall replace the triple libation.”

When the Grand Clarity Palace was first completed, artisans were dispatched to Mount Taibai to quarry white stone for the sacred image of the August Primordial. They also carved an image of the August Ancestor, which was placed to the right, both clad in the robes and crowns of state, adorned with silk and vermilion jade. Later, a jade sculpture of the Lord Lao and the August Ancestor, along with the emperor’s true countenance, was installed in the Palace of the Inaugurated Sage.

On the *gengyin* day of the ninth cycle, the Censor-in-Chief Wang Boye reported that Wang Xuan’yi of Mount Taibai had beheld the August Emperor of the Primordial Mystery within the Treasure Immortal Grotto. He presented a stone casket containing the *Scripture of Supplication for the Protection of the State*, a treasure tally, and other records. The emperor ordered the Minister of Justice, Wang Chui, to retrieve them, and they were subsequently presented to the throne.

On the first day of the first month of the tenth cycle, the *yiyou* day, the emperor personally offered sacrifices at the Grand Clarity Palace. On the *guisi* day, he performed the ancestral rites at the Grand Temple, and on the *jiawu* day, he conducted the sacrifices to heaven and earth at the southern suburban altar.

In the eleventh cycle, the *renchen* year, famine struck the Three Mountains, killing fifteen or sixteen out of every ten. Many survived by eating wild kudzu and mountain yams. Suddenly, two azure lads descended into the courtyard of the female Daoist Wang Fajin of Jian Prefecture. They declared: “The Great Emperor, recognizing your innate immortal bones and your unwavering devotion to the Dao, has commanded us to escort you to the Upper Capital to receive your duties.”

Wang Fajin unconsciously rose into the void, ascending directly to the imperial presence. Now, when the Venerable Lord governs the Ten Heavens and oversees the myriad people, he is called the Heavenly August Great Emperor Radiant-Soul Treasure. Thereupon, Wang Fajin prostrated in audience. The Venerable Lord offered her a draught of rosy nectar and gently addressed her: “When the people of the world spurn the five grains, they incur the censure of the celestial spirits. You must return to the world and admonish the common folk, urging them to repent of their transgressions.” He then commanded his attendant maidens to present her with a scroll of *The Numinous Treasure Rites of Purificatory Fasting and Thanksgiving to Heaven and Earth*, to be transmitted throughout the world. He declared: “Let them gather in secluded places upon lofty mountains to perform fasts and repent of their sins, and their past karmic burdens shall be dissolved. The spirits of the grain father and silkworm mother will then bestow abundance.” “In the year of the Dragon and Tiger, I shall summon you again.” With that, he sent her back. The present *Heavenly Lord’s Fast* observed in Shu is this very rite.

In the twelfth cycle, Wang Fajin once more ascended to heaven. In the thirteenth cycle, on the *guiyou* day of the second month, the emperor personally offered sacrifices at the Grand Clarity Palace and bestowed upon the Sacred Ancestor, the Mysterious Origin Emperor, the august title *Great Sacred Ancestor, Supreme Great Dao, Golden Watchtower, Mysterious Origin, Heavenly August Great Emperor*. He decreed that the officials should henceforth perform the rites of offering and incense-burning on the four seasonal beginnings and the five *la* festivals, and that all prefectures and counties under heaven should perpetually follow this model.

In the fifteenth cycle, the emperor toured Shu. The Mysterious Origin [Lord] appeared by the Blackwater River in Sanquan County of Hanzhong Prefecture, and the emperor personally paid reverence. He then commanded that a stone likeness of the true countenance be carved at the site, six *li* south of Qinwang Post Station. Later, in Yichang County of Lizhou, atop a mountain ridge, the Venerable Lord was seen riding a white deer. Suddenly, the deer shed its antlers, transforming into a white stag, thereby foretelling the suppression of [An] Lushan’s rebellion. By imperial edict, the mountain was named White Guard Ridge, and a *Ziran* Abbey was established at the site of the apparition.

In his youth, Li Bi harbored aspirations for immortality and once journeyed to Mount Song to seek Daoist arts. The Venerable Lord instructed Anqi Sheng to admonish him, saying: “The dynastic fortune is imperiled, and the times are fraught with calamity. You should aid the sovereign with civil and martial arts, broadly succoring the living, and only then may you cast off the mortal coil and ascend in transcendence.” Li Bi thereupon returned and assisted Emperor Suzong in quelling the rebellion and restoring the royal house. He served three reigns in succession before transforming into an immortal.

According to the *Extensive Records of the Taiping Era*: Li Bi’s mother, née Zhou, carried him in her womb for three years before giving birth, and he was born with hair down to his brows. As a child, he was so light that he could stand atop a screen. A Daoist remarked: “This boy will ascend to heaven in broad daylight at the age of fifteen.” Strange fragrances and celestial music would sometimes arise, and colored clouds would hang upon the trees in his courtyard. His family then prepared garlic and ginger, commanding someone to climb onto the roof and scatter them.

Later, while traveling to Mount Song and Mount Heng, he encountered Master Tongxiang, Master Xianmen, and Master Anqi, who taught him the arts of longevity, feathered transcendence, and alchemical ingestion. They admonished him: “By the command of the Supreme, the dynastic fortune is in peril, and the court faces many trials. You should aid the sovereign with civil and martial arts, ensuring your merit extends to the living, and only then may you ascend in transcendence and cast off the mortal coil.” Thereafter, he often abstained from grains and ingested *qi*, cultivating the essentials of the Yellow Emperor and Laozi’s *Valley Spirit*.

In the eighth year of the Tianbao era, while staying at the home of his cousin Zheng Shuze, Li Bi suddenly fell into a deep slumber. His body then emerged from the crown of his head, two or three *cun* in length, with attendant immortals waving their hands and moving their eyes as if assisting. When his feet nearly reached the top of his head, he thought: “The great task is not yet complete, and I still cherish my family.” He then willed himself to return, and those beside him dispersed. He saw a figure of immense stature, clad in imperial robes, before whom a woman in ceremonial dress knelt. The imperial figure reproached him: “Though I knew you were not yet ready, I still summoned you, troubling the host of divine immortals.” The kneeling woman replied: “Not so. It would be better to instruct him to draw near the Son of Heaven.” He then awoke.

In the tenth year, Emperor Xuanzong summoned him to court, where he composed *The August Tang Dynastic Fortune* and lectured on the *Daodejing*. The emperor decreed that he should be as a commoner among the crown prince and the princes. Yang Guozhong, envious of him, banished him to the famous mountains. When An Lushan seized Tong Pass, Emperors Xuanzong and Suzong divided their routes to tour the realm, and Prince Wang was appointed military commissioner of the He-Luo region. Someone found Li Bi between Mount Song and Mount Shaoshi, and upon receiving a handwritten letter from Emperor Suzong, Prince Wang immediately provided carriages and horses to send him to Lingwu. Emperor Suzong received him both within and without the palace, consulting him on all matters, great and small. They slept on adjacent couches and rode side by side when traveling.

Once, while discussing the merits and rewards of the generals, Li Bi remarked: “If I may speak of my own wishes, they differ from those of others.” The emperor asked: “How so?” Li Bi replied: “I abstain from grains and have no family. Rank and fief are of no concern to me. I only wish to sleep with my head upon the emperor’s knee, so that the officials may report that a guest star has trespassed upon the imperial seat.” The emperor laughed heartily.

During the southern sojourn to Fufeng, at each halt, the emperor would order Li Bi to lead the marshal’s troops ahead, inspect the lodgings, secure the keys, and submit reports before the imperial carriage arrived at Baoding Prefecture. Li Bi, somewhat fatigued, dozed off in his quarters. When the emperor arrived, he did not disturb him but instead climbed onto the bed and cradled Li Bi’s head in his lap. After a long while, Li Bi awoke, and the emperor said: “You have now rested upon the Son of Heaven’s knee. When shall the recovery of the realm be achieved?” Li Bi hastily rose and apologized: “In my estimation, by the numinous power of the Nine Ancestral Temples and the might of Your Majesty, it shall be as the name of this prefecture suggests—soon to be pacified and stabilized.” Within ten days, the armies of the Western Regions, Hexi, and Jiang-Huai, along with the corvée laborers, arrived in succession, and the two capitals were recovered.

When Li Bi dwelled in the mountains, he dwelt in secluded forests, aloof from worldly affairs. When he served at court, his secret strategies and upright counsel always accorded with the mysterious workings of the Dao. Thus, across four reigns, his favor and distinction were unparalleled. Yet such men as Yuan Zai and Li Fuguo regarded him as an enemy.

When Emperor Daizong ascended the throne, he repeatedly bestowed gifts upon Li Bi. Imperial messengers crowded the roads, proclaiming him "Master of the Central Peak at Tianzhu Peak." He was granted the *Chaotian Jade Tablet* and, upon his passing, posthumously honored as Grand Mentor to the Crown Prince. That same month, the imperial messenger Lin Yuan encountered Li Bi at an inn near Blue Pass—riding alone in plain clothes, briefly bound for Mount Hua. They spoke of affairs across three reigns, their sorrow lingering long before parting. Upon reaching Chang’an, Lin Yuan learned of his death. When Emperor Dezong heard the news, his grief was profound.

Thus was fulfilled the saying that Li Bi had aided four sagely rulers and escaped calamity. The Daoist Wang Faming of Kuizhou was born with an abnormally long tongue, rendering his speech unclear. After entering the Dao, he recited the *Daodejing* daily. Years later, he suddenly dreamed of Lord Lao trimming his tongue. Upon waking, his speech was corrected.

On the eighteenth day of the third month in the ding-you year of the Zhide era (757 CE), the people of Tonghua Commandery gathered at Cloud Dragon Crag to pray for the nation’s fortune, holding a grand fast. Suddenly, auspicious clouds and strange fragrances arose, lingering without dissipating. After some time, they gradually parted, revealing divine radiance illuminating the sky. There stood Lord Lao before the mountain, his form bridging earth and heaven. Though the mountain was tall, it reached no higher than his elbow. His left hand hung down, while his right held a *Fivefold Luminous Fan*, his majestic presence resplendent.

The assembled multitude gazed in reverence, and after a long while, he vanished. A full report was promptly submitted, and an imperial decree ordered the event depicted in paintings.

The Supreme August High Emperor composed a eulogy with preface, saying: "Our Great Sage Ancestor, born to unfold the manifold mysteries, illumined the Upper Clarity, bequeathing wisdom to his descendants and repeatedly manifesting subtle aid. By day, he appeared in wondrous form, auspicious hues floating in the void. Clad in raiment of the Seven Luminaries and Fivefold Brilliance, attended by jade lads and golden maidens, he drew homage from Daoists, Buddhists, humans, and devas alike. In former times, the *Zhen’gao* was transmitted at Yangjiao, ensuring the imperial line’s boundless endurance; today, his august presence shines upon Dragon Crag, and inauspicious vapors shall soon vanish. Not merely has this been a transmission across generations, whereby former kings attained the One—it is also a sign of blessings bestowed upon the ancestral temple and state, ensuring ten thousand generations. We command that this be rendered in elegant brushwork and displayed throughout the commanderies and kingdoms. Beholding it beneath the vast heavens shall be as standing in the Hall of the Supreme Ultimate."

Eulogy:
"August was our illustrious ancestor,
Who expounded the teaching in due time.
Governing body and state alike,
He declared: ‘Seek the sunlit level plain.’
Above, he opened the grottoes of immortals;
Below, he beheld the divine countenance.
Radiant was the perfect Dao,
Its counsel ever non-action.
The cliffs and valleys grew resplendent,
Beyond the reach of cinnabar and ink.
Divine light flickered,
Auspicious daylight lingered.
The court rejoiced,
All commanderies came to witness.
Blessings and prosperity flowed forth,
A thousand ages dwelling here."

In the second year of the Qianyuan era (759 CE), on a *jihai* day, the Emperor dreamed of two azure lads leading him to a palace, where he was granted an audience with Lord Lao. Crowned with a Nine-Phoenix Diadem and robed in cloud-and-rosy-gauze attire, his beard and hair were black. Leaning upon a jade armrest and holding a whisk, he was attended by a vast retinue of perfected ones, lads, jade maidens, and divine warriors. The Emperor, clad in crimson robes and holding a ritual tablet, stood in attendance behind him. They traversed mountains and seas, journeying great distances. At dawn, he summoned images for comparison and found that in the Hall of the Sage Ancestor at the Guangtian Abbey in Wuguang Ward, there indeed stood a statue of Lord Lao with black hair, exactly as seen in the dream. Overjoyed, the Emperor had his own imperial portrait painted and placed standing behind the statue. He then issued an edict commanding its veneration throughout the realm.

On the fifteenth day of the eighth month in the fifth year of the Dali era (770 CE), Emperor Daizong turned to his ministers and asked: "Is the matter of divine immortals credible?" Li Fan replied: "The notion of divine immortals originates with the Daoists, whose teachings are founded upon the *Laozi*’s five thousand words. The *Laozi*’s essential message differs not from the classics. Later generations, fond of the strange, falsely attributed tales of divine immortals to Laozi.
