These mark and illuminate the statutes, depicting the workings of creation, thereby proclaiming boundless benefit, aiding the great harmony of the cosmos, serving as the guideposts of the sagely teachings, and directing the senses of all sentient beings. Having received the primordial mandate, We nurture the multitudes, hoping to broaden the true canon and silently nourish all beings.

The *Scripture of the Heavenly Youth for the Protection of Life* is a secret revelation of the Supreme Clarity, a precious talisman of the Golden Portal. It has long been attested in earlier records and disseminated in separate catalogues. Should one purify the heart and recite it, or focus the mind and uphold it, one may surely dispel plagues and repel evil, attain harmony and longevity—akin to the *Scriptures of Fuxi* in establishing symbols to subtly assist the numinous, or like the *Xia Tripods* in banishing demons, so that one encounters no *chimei* spirits, averts calamities from the six extremes, and gathers blessings from a hundred auspices. Thus, We have had it transcribed for promulgation and prefaced it with this introduction. May all within the seas together delight in the blessings of life and growth.

Earlier, as the imperial heir remained long unborn, the Emperor commanded Daoist Zhu Ziying of Mount Juqu to present a memorial. Ziying, with single-minded sincerity, ascended in spirit to the imperial throne and suddenly beheld the Three Lords of Maoshan each riding a precious carriage, descending along the Yellow Way. Ziying prostrated himself to make way, whereupon he heard one among the carriages ask: "Why have you come here?" Ziying replied: "I have come to beseech the August Supreme on behalf of the Emperor Zhenzong for a sagely heir." The Mao Lord assented, saying: "This is indeed a great matter among men." Soon after, the memorial was presented to the Supreme Lord, who decreed: "The Maos possess a heart that grieves for the state and cherishes the people; they shall grant the Song Son of Heaven an heir." The following year, a royal prince was indeed born—this was Emperor Renzong.

In the early Tiansheng era, Ziying was summoned to court, where the Two August Ones held him in the highest esteem, bestowing upon him the title *Master of Observing the Wondrous*. The Qianyuan and Tiansheng Observatories were built to honor his merit. According to the *Inscription on the Stele of Master Zhu, the Twenty-Second Patriarch of Mount Maoshan and Master of Observing the Wondrous*:

> When the third generation of the imperial line bore auspicious omens,
> And the Spring Minister’s post lay vacant,
> Sacrifices were offered to the high and distant,
> While the Grotto-Heaven’s Controller of Destiny withdrew his friendship.

This refers to the events above.

In the fourth year of Emperor Renzong’s *Celestial Protection* (1026), the chief minister Wang Zeng remarked that among the scriptures of the *Daoist Canon*, some contained language that was coarse and vulgar. The Emperor replied: "The *Daoist Canon* contains many discourses on refining elixirs and compounding medicines—how could they all be like the *Five Thousand Words* of Laozi?"

Chief Minister Zhang Zhibai remarked: "The *Scripture on the Dao and Its Virtue* is the guardian of purity and quiescence—it differs from all other Daoist scriptures." The Emperor replied: "When collecting and examining Daoist scriptures today, they must be meticulously collated before being admitted into the Canon."

In the second year of the *Accordant Harmony* reign (1055), on the first month of the year *yiwei*, the Emperor fell gravely ill. He summoned Daoist Liu Congshan of the Jianlong Abbey to the Great Celebration Hall to perform a jiao offering and present memorials, ordering his chief ministers to bow in his stead. As the night deepened and the memorials were being submitted, the Emperor suddenly worsened, his eyes closing for what seemed like hours. Court and kin were thrown into panic. After a long delay, Congshan finally rose and declared: "The memorials have been received. The Most High has issued a decree of deliverance—the imperial carriage returns." Moments later, the Emperor revived. He immediately sent word to ask: "Who is this General Ge?" Congshan replied: "He is the Middle Prime General of the Three Heavens’ Gate, responsible for reviewing memorials." Another edict swiftly followed, commanding that an altar be prepared for offerings.

The next day, the Emperor’s health was fully restored. Those who had witnessed the event later recounted: "From within the gate, a voice declared, ‘The Emperor was not fated to come. Quickly fetch a horse to send him back.’ And so he awoke." By imperial decree, a shrine to General Ge was erected west of the suburban altar, and Congshan was lavished with imperial robes, gold, and silks.

When Fan Zhongyan, Duke of Culture and Rectitude, served as vice-prefect of Chenzhou, the prefect sought Daoists to present memorials for his ailing mother. Fan remarked: "How could a common practitioner convey a memorial to the imperial court?" Yet as he visited the sickbed, he ordered the Daoist to proceed. The man prostrated himself for so long without moving that those present touched his body—he had stiffened. Only at the fifth watch did he rise, telling the prefect: "By the Most High’s decree, the Lady’s lifespan extends six more years. Her suffering need not cause worry." Fan questioned the Daoist about his prolonged prostration. The man replied: "As I returned from submitting the memorial, I chanced upon the celestial assembly reviewing the list of successful candidates for next year’s imperial examination. The immortals had gathered to watch, and the crowd was so dense I could not pass—hence the delay." Fan doubted his tale and asked: "Did you see the list, Master?" "How could I not?" the Daoist replied. "Who is the top candidate?" Fan pressed. The Daoist answered: "His surname is Wang, and his given name is written with *gong* above and another character below, though the lower character is smudged with ink. Another character is inscribed beside it, but the gate of heaven is too high—I could not make it out." The following year, Wang Gongshou indeed topped the examination, and the Emperor’s brush altered his name to Gongchen.

In the seventh year of the *Auspicious Aid* reign (1062), the Emperor fell ill and dreamed of three divine beings who announced their names and titles, flanked by attendants in resplendent array. Upon waking, his illness vanished. He ordered a search for shrines matching their descriptions, but none were found. Later, he discovered their identities in the *Record of the Orthodox Unity of the Most High*: they were the Three Generals. On the sixteenth day of the third month in the eighth year (1063), an edict proclaimed:

> The workings of the divine are most subtle, yet they manifest in the evident. The sincerest devotion reaches even the faintest realms. When resonance and response align as if by design, when the hidden traces of the perfected and the soaring forms of the immortals reveal themselves—then the Tang General, the Supreme Numinous Soaring Spirit; the Ge General, the Direct Envoy of the Flying Perfected; and the Zhou General, the Ascending Immortal of the Celestial Ranks, whose names are inscribed in the registers of the true, must be honored. Recently, when We were afflicted, their numinous aid restored Us to health. Without bestowing noble titles, how could their names be exalted? Without consecrating a secret chamber, how could their majesty be enshrined? Let the Tang General be granted the title *True Lord of Dao Transformation*, the Ge General *True Lord of Upright Protection*, and the Zhou General *True Lord of Resolute Will*. Let halls be built for them within the capital’s abbeys, that their radiant virtue may be fittingly requited.

In the third year of the *Prime Abundance* reign (1080), at the petition of Zhang Junshan, an edict decreed that henceforth, those seeking Daoist office must be examined on the *Scripture on the Dao and Its Virtue*, the *Scripture of the Numinous Treasure’s Salvation of Humankind*, and the *True Scripture of the Southern Florescence*. In the fifth year (1082), the Emperor expanded the titles of divine immortals. Yet another edict forbade the inclusion of the Three Clarities’ Supreme Lords among the ranks of the departed in Buddhist Water and Land Dharma assemblies, deeming it a profanation of the exalted perfected. Local officials were ordered to strictly enforce this prohibition.

On the night of the fifteenth day of the second month in the fifth year of the *Succeeding the Sagely* reign (1098), as the Daoist community of the Great Clarity Abbey in Bozhou gathered for their evening rites, they beheld a crimson radiance emanating from between the eyebrows of the statue of the Venerable Lord Lao. The light gradually filled the hall, piercing the tiled roof and ascending to the heavens, where it entered the Hall of the Primordial Great Sage in the Grotto-Heaven Palace. After lingering, the glow resolved into three paths: two on either side, blazing like rosy clouds, and one in the center, gleaming like a white silk ribbon. Their brilliance stretched unbroken, spanning the sky like a rainbow bridge. For hundreds of *li*, the land was as bright as day. People near and far poured from their homes to gaze upward, burning incense and bowing in reverence. After the second watch, the light slowly shifted and vanished into the Gate of Heaven.

The Abbot Observant Master Zhang Jingxian, along with Daoist adepts such as Han Weiji and a total of one hundred forty persons, and the Abbess of the Grotto-Heaven Palace, the female adept Wang Jingsu, with eighty-one others, submitted their accounts. Likewise, Li Xiang, Supervisor of the Palace and concurrently Supervisor of Liquor Taxes for Guyang Town, along with Wang Jing and one hundred ten other registered townsfolk, presented their testimonies. Prefect Yu Lu of Bozhou and his subordinates also witnessed the marvel of the divine radiance and accordingly memorialized the throne. An imperial edict was issued to hold a Golden Register Daoist ritual at the palace for a full month. Prefect Yu Lu was appointed to represent the court in receiving the mandate, while Jia Shanxiang, Chief Supervisor of the Left Street Daoists, led his subordinates in conducting the rites.

Shanxiang had once visited the Supreme Clarity Palace, where the assembly requested him to expound the *Scripture of Salvation*. By the second fascicle of his discourse, the blind regained their sight. Among the attendees was an elderly woman over seventy, who had lost her vision for thirty years; upon hearing the scriptural meaning, her eyes suddenly brightened. On the evening of the grand offering, Shanxiang dreamed that a host of divine officials transmitted the command of the Supreme Lord Lao, bestowing upon him the vestments of immortality and appointing him as the Abbot of the Supreme Clarity Palace. Several days later, he ascended in transcendence. Zhang Shangying composed the *Record of the True Journey*, which fully documented these events.

On the eighteenth day of the third month, the cyclical day *dingmao*, a blue-green memorial was presented: "The heir apparent, your subject [Name], respectfully dispatches Su Gui, Eunuch Attendant of the Inner Bureau and Supervisor of the Imperial Pharmacy, to request thirty-seven Daoist masters to conduct a month-long rite of prayer and blessing at the Supreme Clarity Palace. Upon its conclusion, a grand universal offering of thirty-six hundred altars shall be held."

The memorial continued: "Your subject humbly invokes the Supreme Lord Lao, the Primordial Emperor of Utmost Virtue, the Jade Sovereign of the Great Clarity: The sacred precincts of Qiao and Bozhou, where the divine truth resides, have manifested auspicious omens—celestial radiance emanating from between the brows, illuminating a thousand realms. Though my virtue is unworthy, I have received this heavenly favor. Day and night, I reverently uphold the rites, daring not to slacken. On the twentieth day, as I ascended the hall to burn incense at dusk, I suddenly beheld a light beneath the eyes of the Venerable Lord Lao, like twin pearls glowing with round brilliance, which persisted until the *si* hour before dissipating. On the ninth day of the fourth month, the pearlescent radiance reappeared as before."

The prefectural congratulatory memorial stated: "...a single strand of light first illuminated the palace hall, its five hues vivid and resplendent, swiftly ascending to the heavens. Flanking it were luminous clouds as lush as festive vapors, while at its center, a white silk ribbon unfurled and coiled. It was said: 'Transformation subtly takes formless shape, and blessings naturally arise from manifest signs.' The extraordinary hues of floating clouds would be deemed a most glorious record by historians, and this manifestation of sacred favor aligns with the boundless fortune of the imperial lineage."

In the fifth month of the fifth year of the *Chongning* era (1106), Emperor Huizong issued an edict: "Those who rule the realm must revere and serve the Supreme Deity. The imperial decrees are most solemn; none dare be irreverent. Yet the followers of Śākya, in their construction of Buddhist rites, recklessly rank the Heavenly Emperor among ghosts and spirits, blurring the distinction between the divine and the spectral—nothing could be more egregious. How can they truly honor the will of the Supreme Deity? Let the relevant authorities investigate and excise such errors to reflect our awe and reverence."

Another decree stipulated: "Within the Water and Land Rituals, the altars of the Three Clarities and the Jade Emperor are established. How can the lofty perfected of the Three Realms be equated with the ghosts of the netherworld? During the *Yuanfeng* era of the late Divine Emperor, an edict was once issued to prohibit such practices. Let this be reinstated and enforced."

A further edict declared: "In the past, many Buddhist monasteries displayed images of the Three Teachings as their hall or courtyard names, with Śākya in the center, the Venerable Lord Lao on the left, and Confucius on the right. This does not accord with the court’s intent to honor the celestial deities and promote Confucian teachings. Let the Venerable Lord Lao and the meritorious deeds of Daoism be relocated to Daoist temples, and let the Sage Confucius be moved to local academies, to rectify names and distinguish the teachings."

On the fourth day of the first month of the first year of the *Daguan* era (1107), the Ministry of Rites issued a memorandum in accordance with the decree: "Daoist priests shall be ranked above Buddhist monks, and female Daoist adepts above Buddhist nuns."

In the second year of the *Zhihe* era (1112), in Jiankang Prefecture, a villager named Liang Guangying had long suffered from leprosy. Fearing contagion, his family abandoned him. He took refuge at the Jade Dawn Abbey on Mount Mao, dedicating himself to hauling water for the Daoist community by day and sleeping beneath the Dragon-Tiger Lords at the abbey’s triple gate by night. After several years of such devotion, one day as he drew water, an elder with white hair and plain robes, riding a white horse with crimson mane, appeared amidst purple mist. His body radiated light, illuminating the mountains and rivers. Before him, two attendants bearing tablets shouted: 'The Supreme Lord Lao approaches!' Liang prostrated himself and kowtowed. The Venerable Lord said: 'The *Wondrous Scripture of the Heavenly Youth for Protecting Life* has circulated in the world for ages. Have you heard of it?' Liang replied: 'I have not.' The Lord said: 'I now bestow it upon you. Memorize it, recite it while drawing water for bathing, and your illness shall be cured. You may also use it to aid others.' He then recited the scripture, which is the *Wondrous Scripture of the Heavenly Youth for Protecting Life* known in the world today."

In the eighth month of the sixth year (1116), an edict was issued: "The Supreme Lord Lao, the Primordial Emperor of Utmost Virtue, bears the name *Er* and the style *Boyang*, with the sobriquet *Li*; these are recorded in the classics and transmitted texts. Many among the gentry and commoners today use them as personal names, which is deeply irreverent. Henceforth, such usage is strictly prohibited."

In the eleventh month, an imperial pronouncement declared: "When the Zhou dynasty declined, a sage emerged in China, composing a work of eighty-one chapters to bequeath to later generations. Serene and solitary, he dwelled with the divine—how could one fathom him? The Han historians Sima Qian and Ban Gu, with their petty intellects and self-serving motives, composed biographies that equated him with the likes of Han Fei and Shen Buhai. In their *Tables of Ancient and Modern Personages*, they ranked him in the third tier, below Ziyou and Zixia. Such disparagement is now rectified. The *Records of the Grand Historian* shall elevate the *Biography of Laozi* to the foremost position among the biographies, forming its own category. The *Tables of Ancient and Modern Personages* in the *Book of Han* shall reclassify him among the Supreme Sages. All extant editions shall be corrected accordingly."

Yesterday, in annotating the *Scripture of the Dao and Its Virtue*, it was decreed to follow the Tang precedent: let eminent ministers divide it into chapters and verses, transcribe it, and inscribe it upon stone at the Divine Empyrean Longevity Palace in the capital, to endure for eternity."

The *Subtleties of the Records of the Grand Historian* by Sima Zhen faults Sima Qian for placing the biographies of Laozi and Han Fei together, arguing that their teachings diverge entirely and should not share a single account. As the ancients have already established, his preface states: "Boyang’s teaching is pure and vacuous, while Hanzi’s is severe and legalistic; their stillness and agitation differ, and their virtue and punishment clash." Now, it is fitting that the Keeper of the Archives be paired with the Master of the Varnished Garden in a shared biography, just as the Duke of Zhou is ranked alongside Shang Yang—how could this not be excellent? The present edict elevates him to the foremost position among the biographies, forming his own category, which is even more perfect.

Furthermore, Ban Gu’s *Tables of Ancient and Modern Personages* in the *Book of Han* divides figures into nine ranks, yet places Laozi in the third. The Later Han edict of Bian Zhao states: "Ban Gu deemed Laozi’s rejection of sagacity and wisdom as the root of disorder, and thus ranked him below Confucius, whose Way is all-encompassing. This suppression placed him in the same category as Zixi of Chu." These two assessments differ greatly—truly, "those whose Ways diverge do not consult one another." It also states: "The measure of a great person transcends common judgment; how could the nine ranks constrain his name?" Lu Xisheng of the Tang likewise remarked: "Confucius personally met Laozi and inquired of him regarding ritual—there is no doubt of this. Yet Ban Gu demoted him to the third rank; though his name may be demoted, can his Way be diminished?" These are the public judgments of the world.

Thus, the Illustrious Emperor of the Tang once issued an edict elevating Laozi to the rank of Supreme Sage in the *Records of the Grand Historian*. Now, this dynasty issues a similar decree—truly, "the principles of former and later sages are one." On the twentieth day, a proclamation declared: "The Dao is present in all things. Since the Han, it has been artificially divided, and the world has drifted into vulgarity, failing to perceive its wholeness—hence its obscurity. We now renew and restore it, investigating its origins, so that the teachings of the Yellow Emperor, Laozi, Yao, Shun, Zhou, and Confucius may flourish together in this age." Let all students in the empire’s schools add one major and one minor classic to their studies, choosing as they wish. The major classics shall be the *Yellow Emperor’s Inner Canon* and the *Scripture of the Dao and Its Virtue*; the minor classics, the *Zhuangzi* and the *Liezi*.

Henceforth, those who study the Dao and seek admission to the schools shall be examined by their local prefectures and counties, with guarantees provided. Those who have not committed punishable offenses, the Ten Abominations, theft, or violated the Eight Virtues shall be permitted to enter the prefectural and county schools for instruction, following the existing educational statutes. Their primary texts shall be the *Yellow Emperor’s Inner Canon* and the *Scripture of the Dao and Its Virtue* as major classics, and the *Zhuangzi* and *Liezi* as minor classics, supplemented by Confucian works to achieve synthesis. The Daoist classics shall include the *Book of Changes* as a major classic and the *Mencius* as a minor classic.

Previously, only titles such as Master, Dharma Master, Recluse, and Grand Master existed, with few official ranks. As their designations were lofty, their official status should likewise be elevated, though advancement remained difficult. In addition to the existing system, those selected from among the students may be appointed according to the following ranks and grades:

- **Primary Gentleman (元士)**: Principal Grade 5
- **Exalted Gentleman (高士)**: Auxiliary Grade 5
- **Great Gentleman (大士)**: Principal Grade 6
- **Superior Gentleman (上士)**: Auxiliary Grade 6
- **Virtuous Gentleman (良士)**: Principal Grade 7
- **Square Gentleman (方士)**: Auxiliary Grade 7
- **Secluded Gentleman (逸士)**: Principal Grade 8
- **Dwelling Gentleman (居士)**: Auxiliary Grade 8
- **Hidden Gentleman (隐士)**: Principal Grade 9
- **Aspiring Gentleman (志士)**: Auxiliary Grade 9

Their salaries and allowances shall follow the regulations for officials of corresponding ranks. The Divine Empyrean Longevity Palace, the Heavenly Celebration Abbey, and other palaces and abbeys shall appoint their superintendents and deputies from among those who have passed the school examinations, with the Ministry of Rites maintaining registers and making appointments in accordance with the Ministry of Personnel’s procedures. For those recluses dwelling in mountains and forests, the surveillance commissioners and prefectural governors shall, in accordance with the Eight Virtues, extend invitations to the prefectural schools and report their names.

Thereafter, Minister of Rites Xue Sichang memorialized that the Ministry of Rites should issue stamped documents to the relevant offices, and the request was approved. On the same day, an edict decreed: "Let images of Zhuang Zhou and Lie Yukou be installed in the Divine Empyrean Longevity Palace and enshrined alongside the Most High, to reflect Our reverence for the subtleties of the Dao." This shall be recorded in the *Annals of the Former Sages’ Governance*.

The editorial official Wang Li stated: "The merits of Zhuangzi and Liezi are no less than those of Yan [Hui] and Meng [zi]. Yet while the court honors Confucius and enshrines Yan and Meng as his attendants, bestowing upon them the rank of duke, Zhuang and Lie are merely classified among the Hundred Schools—no special distinction has been granted. We humbly request that the rites of veneration be deliberated." Thus, the present proclamation was issued.

On the ninth day of the sixth month of the first year of the Xuanhe era, an edict declared: "Let Zhuang Zhou be enfeoffed as the True Lord of Subtle Wonder and Penetrating Dao, and Lie Yukou as the True Lord of Attaining Vacuity and Observing Wonder," and the investiture was carried out. In the eighth month, the editorial officials of the Daoist history reported that the compilation of the *Daoist History* had reached its temporal limit. An edict decreed that the *Daoist History* should conclude with the Five Dynasties, while the present dynasty’s records should form the *Daoist Canon*.

On the third day of the eleventh month of the third year of the Xuanhe era, an edict directed the Supervisor of the Daoist Registry, currently compiling the *Daoist History*, to recognize that this work transcends ordinary historiography. While the formats of the *Records of the Grand Historian* and the *Book of Han* may offer models, the *Tables* section shall not be included as a mere formality. The *Annals of the Dao* shall commence with the separation of Heaven and Earth, placing the Three Pure Ones at the forefront. The sage-kings who attained the Dao shall follow the Three Sovereigns in chronological order. Twelve treatises shall be established: Heaven, Earth, Palaces and Offices, Ranks and Appointments, Chariots and Attire, Talismans and Registers, Rituals and Norms, Prohibitions and Laws, Cultivation and Refinement, Elixirs and Minerals, Sacred Writings, and Treasured Scriptures.

The biographies of male perfected beings shall begin with Feng Hou and Li Mu, while those of female perfected beings shall commence with the Nine Numinous Ones and the Primordial Lady. The biographies of all other commoners who attained the Dao shall be arranged in chronological order.

The *Annals of the Later Sage Lord Li of the Golden Portal*, composed by the Azure Lad of the Square Palaces, states: "When the two forces of darkness and light converge, the ordering of things follows its time; when the two Ways wax and wane, their emergence and withdrawal depend on the turning of fate. When the time arrives, one adapts accordingly; when the turning comes, one embraces it. In the years following the Tang, forty-six *dinghai* cycles passed, and thereafter another fifty-six *dinghai* cycles occurred. During this interval, rulers bore names of ninefold and unitary schemes. In the first year of the Jian’guang and Yanchang eras, and in the subsequent *jiashen* year, those who planted goodness and eliminated the suffering of the people, who dispelled plagues and floods, whose lands were engulfed by deluges above and ravaged by war below—all evil was eradicated, and all calamities vanished."

Those devoted to the Dao withdrew into seclusion, while the virtuous ascended the mountains. On the sixth day of the third month in the *renchen* year, the Golden Portal Sage Lord descended, his radiance illuminating the multitudes. At that time, the Sage Lord set forth from Mount Qingcheng, emerging from the clouded north of Longxi, his gaze extending beyond the realm of the Torch Dragon.

North of the Black Lands of the North lies a mountain, towering so high it brushes the heavens, its peaks locked in perpetual ice and snow, where daylight never appears. Yet when one faces north, the darkness grows brighter; gazing upward at night, one beholds the North Pole, the abode of the Torch Dragon. The Torch Dragon is the spirit of the North. As the *Classic of Mountains and Seas* states: "Beyond the northwestern sea dwells a deity with the face of a man and the body of a serpent, clad in red. When darkness falls, its eyes shine; it neither eats nor sleeps. It is the Illuminator of the Nine Yin, called the Torch Dragon, whose light can illuminate all."

Turning westward, he passed the Pass of the Nine Streams, then eastward to the dawn-lit groves of Fulin. Gazing south toward Mount Zhu, he rode through the void in a threefold white flying chariot, followed by a host of ten thousand dragons from the emptiness. Heavenly light bathed all in its glow, and the divine mirror of the Three Luminaries was revealed. Evil men were extinguished in water and fire, while the compassionate and good were preserved as the seed of the people.

Those who first embarked on the path became immortals; those who attained the Dao became immortal officials. If one could refine the Grotto Chamber in the Upper Prime, cultivate the Nine Perfected with unceasing diligence, traverse the Hidden Scriptures of the Seven Spirits, and exhaust the Eight Simplicities with sincerity, then one would traverse the Three Calamities unharmed and surely witness renewal in the Great Peace. One would then be granted scriptures to become an immortal official, attaining long life as a divine perfected.

Thereafter, the Sage Lord would further select the most refined and wondrous among them, promoting them to fill the ranks of officials. Some would be appointed as Immortal Earls, others as Immortal Marquises, assisting the Sage in shepherding the people, ordering *qi*, and spreading virtue. Some would govern a single district, others be entrusted with the governance of an entire state. Those who could invoke the sun with solemn rites, bind the moon with lunar hymns, ascend the Great Grotto’s heights, master the Seven Transformations’ revolving verses, recite the true scriptures of the Golden Portal, wear the great talismans of the Divine Tiger, deploy the Eight Ways to summon spirits, open the Purple Writ to ride the floating clouds, chant the Golden Root to endure forever, set forth the Nine Reds to seal the mounds, command the Curved Simplicity to summon spirits, and employ the Purple Measure to manifest the unseen—those who could don the Five Phases to summon demons, embrace the Jade Tablets without cease, pass through trials and ordeals without doubt, and tread through weapons and fire without fear—all such would be appointed as Left and Right Immortal Dukes, Left and Right Grand Masters, or as ministers in the courts of the immortal marquises of the Upper States.

The Sage Lord’s procession of ten thousand dragons from the void was to observe the multitude of immortals and appoint them according to their talents. Though the Sage Lord was entrusted with governing the multitudes and gazing down upon all living beings, he himself roamed freely from the Golden Portal, dwelling in the palaces of the Upper Clarity, resting his form in the Great Void, wandering the Five Cities, and surveying the Ten Heavens, bringing peace to the hundred regions.

All who witnessed the Great Peace were those of compassionate hearts and benevolent natures, who upheld goodness without cease—whether scholars of the Dao cultivating truth, those worthy of instruction, or spirit-mediums who received scriptures, preserved their essence, and guarded their spiritual embryos; whether those who attained the Dao and became immortals, men of utmost sincerity; or those whose names were recorded in the Mysterious Register, whose seven generations bore virtue, whose blessings extended to their descendants, destined to become immortals; or those born with azure bones, able to commune with spirits and connect with the perfected; or those of extraordinary talent and serene disposition, whose heavenly endowment was pure and surpassing, who were utterly loyal, utterly filial, utterly upright, utterly incorruptible—such were the ranks of immortals, numbering in the hundreds, high and low.

The Sage Lord appointed them all according to their talents, establishing them as greater or lesser Immortal Marquises, each with their own ranks, to govern the seed of the people. Each year, the Immortal Marquises would ascend to the Upper Clarity to present themselves before the Sage Lord and receive their duties. Every five years, the Sage Lord would descend to tour the realm, visiting the Immortal Marquises, inspecting the seed of the people, and examining the governance of the immortals.

For Lao Jun would personally descend in the coming kalpa to become the True Lord of Great Peace, and thus was also titled the Golden Portal Posterior Sage Lord. In the world, when memorials were presented and petitions submitted, when dew-written memorials and written pleas were offered, all beseeched the August Jade Emperor of the Supreme Clarity, the Supreme Elder Lord of the Great Dao, the Golden Portal Posterior Sage Lord of Great Peace. For Lao Jun was the lord of the twelve hundred officials and the twelve hundred official petitions. When sealing petitions, the seal of the Nine Elder Immortal Capital Lords was used, for Lao Jun was also titled the Nine Elder Immortal Capital Lord.

For the most advanced adepts, who stilled their minds and focused their intentions, responses came in accord with their prayers. The immediacy of spiritual resonance, manifesting in sight and sound, recorded in these annals, was but a speck of dust in the vast earth. His circulation through the Three Realms, his boundless salvation of beings—sometimes revealing immortal forms and auspicious signs, even assuming fleshly bodies; sometimes flying, sometimes walking; sometimes exalted, sometimes humble; sometimes in court, sometimes in the wilds; sometimes in the Central Lands, sometimes among the barbarians—when he responded, he would conceal himself, beyond all measure. His coming was without origin, his going without destination; he pervaded all that was and was not, encompassing all things. His true body and transformed bodies alike returned to wondrous being. Praise could not reach him, nor records fully capture him.

Here, we have gathered accounts from scriptures and histories, compiling them into this *Veritable Record*.

*The Ninth Scroll of the Sacred Records of the Primordial Sage concludes.*
